201509	811	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We’ll begin with David Wilcox.	11	1
201509	812	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Thank you, Madam Chair.	11	1
201509	813	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	I will be referring to the packet titled “Material for the US Outlook.”	11	1
201509	814	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The news since the July Tealbook torqued our assessment of the two legs of your policy mandate in different directions.	11	1
201509	815	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	On the real-activity side, we now see the economy as having been operating, and likely to continue to operate, at a higher level of resource utilization than we thought at the time of your July meeting.	11	1
201509	816	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	This reassessment combines four main categories of information.	11	1
201509	817	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	First, as you can see in panel 1 of your forecast summary exhibit, real GDP growth now appears to have been considerably stronger during the first half of this year than we thought at the time of your July meeting.	11	1
201509	818	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Second, the most recent indicators, including yesterday’s encouraging report on retail sales, suggest that some of that greater momentum has carried over into the second half of this year.	11	1
201509	819	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	In particular, taking on board the stronger retail sales news, which is not reflected in your exhibit, we’ve marked up our forecast for current- quarter GDP growth about ½ percentage point relative to the July Tealbook and now have it at about 2¼ percent.	11	1
201509	820	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Third, we interpreted the two labor market reports that were issued during the intermeeting period to be a little stronger than we had expected.	11	1
201509	821	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The August unemployment rate, at 5.1 percent, was 0.2 percentage point lower than we had expected.	11	1
201509	822	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The average monthly gain in payroll employment over the past three months is currently reported to have been 220,000, essentially the same as our July Tealbook forecast; however, in line with the average experience in recent years, we expect the first estimate of job gains in August to be revised up about 60,000.	11	1
201509	823	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Fourth, we have also, of course, noted the more-restrictive turn in some of the key variables that shape our outlook, including the decline in equity prices, the higher path for the exchange value of the dollar, and the less-robust outlook for foreign economic activity, and we have tempered our GDP growth outlook in light of these changes.	11	1
201509	824	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	All told, as Missaka showed in his pre-FOMC briefing yesterday, the adjustments we made in response to these four sources of information result in an output gap that is about ¾ percentage point tighter than before in the second quarter of this year, and we have essentially carried that greater tightness into our projection through the next two years.	11	1
201509	825	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	By 2018, a faster pace of monetary normalization begins to gain some traction and the delta in the GDP gap begins to narrow.	11	1
201509	826	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	As a check on our judgmental thinking, panel 3 compares our judgmental estimate of the output gap with a couple of purely model-based estimates that I have shown the Committee before.	11	1
201509	827	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The dotted blue line shows our Tealbook estimate of the output gap.	11	1
201509	828	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The red line shows the production-function variant of the output gap from the EDO model, which is one of our DSGE models.	11	1
201509	829	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The black line shows the estimate that comes out of a state-space model embedded in the FRB/US model.	11	1
201509	830	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	This FRB/US estimate is developed by pooling a range of real-side indicators including GDP, GDI, and the unemployment rate.	11	1
201509	831	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The model also includes a New Keynesian Phillips curve with anchored expectations, in an effort to sharpen the model’s inference of the natural rate of unemployment and the level of potential GDP.	11	1
201509	832	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	These three estimates—our judgmental assessment and the two model-based estimates—are unanimous in taking the view that resource utilization has just about returned to its maximum sustainable position.	11	1
201509	833	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	However, before anyone takes too much comfort from the unanimity among these three estimates, I would note that other models in use around the System give markedly different answers.	11	1
201509	834	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	For example, the Federal Reserve Bank of Philadelphia’s PRISM model shows a GDP gap in the second quarter of nearly 7 percent, and one of the models maintained at New York shows a gap of a little more than 2 percent.	11	1
201509	835	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Also, even the confidence interval that I’m showing here around the FRB/US estimate extends about 2 percentage points in either direction, and that confidence interval surely understates our ignorance because it sets aside both parameter uncertainty and model uncertainty.	11	1
201509	836	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	One important judgmental adjustment in the Tealbook forecast this time around pertained to the unemployment rate.	11	1
201509	837	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	If we had maintained the supply-side assumptions that were embedded in our July forecast and put through our normal translation of the adverse changes in the key environmental variables that I mentioned earlier, we would have shown an unemployment rate that was flat or even rising a touch from its current level.	11	1
201509	838	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Considering the ongoing pace of improvement in labor market conditions, that did not seem the most plausible baseline forecast.	11	1
201509	839	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	To accommodate some further reduction in the unemployment rate, we needed to widen the differential between actual GDP growth and potential GDP growth.	11	1
201509	840	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	In the context of our Okun’s law framework, it didn’t matter much how that wider differential was achieved, but because we were already at the very low end of the spectrum of outside analysts in terms of our forecast for GDP growth, we split the difference and shaved one-tenth or so from our forecast of potential GDP growth in the period ahead and added one-tenth or so to our forecast of actual GDP growth.	11	1
201509	841	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Even with this judgmental add factor, our GDP forecast remains near the pessimistic end of the range of outside forecasters.	11	1
201509	842	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Let me now turn to the inflation leg of your mandate.	11	1
201509	843	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Our forecast here is summarized in panels 4 and 5 of your exhibit.	11	1
201509	844	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	As you can see from panel 4, we now expect total PCE inflation to turn slightly negative in the fourth quarter on a quarterly-average basis, reflecting a steeper decline in consumer energy prices that in turn results from the lower projected path for crude oil prices.	11	1
201509	845	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	We have also edged down our near-term projection of core inflation—panel 5—in response to slightly weaker-than-expected incoming data and a downward revision to our forecast for imported goods prices.	11	1
201509	846	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Over the remainder of the medium term, our projections of both total and core inflation are essentially the same as in July.	11	1
201509	847	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	This morning’s CPI release, which is summarized in a separate exhibit titled “Material for Consumer Price Index Update,” had no material implications relative to our Tealbook expectations.	11	1
201509	848	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Although the core CPI inflation rate was several basis points softer than we had expected, that had little implication for our assessment of PCE inflation, partly because some of the surprise was in airfares and medical care prices, neither of which feed into the PCE price index, and partly because the small downward surprise in housing prices receives a smaller weight in the PCE index than it does in the CPI.	11	1
201509	849	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The increase in financial market volatility during the intermeeting period affected the baseline through channels that have been standard in macro models for decades— mainly, lower stock prices feeding into a wealth effect, higher private borrowing rates, and a stronger dollar.	11	1
201509	850	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	But if we learned anything from the financial crisis, it has to be that disturbances originating in the financial sector can have serious implications for the real economy reaching far beyond these standard channels.	11	1
201509	851	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Marco Del Negro and Marc Giannoni at the Federal Reserve Bank of New York have been working with one of the more interesting recent models that aims to allow a more meaningful role for financial disturbances to affect real outcomes.	11	1
201509	852	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	To shed light on the potential implications of a more serious and protracted version of the turbulence that surfaced last month, they were kind enough to generate one of the alternative simulations that we presented in the Tealbook.	11	1
201509	853	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	In their model, the Baa bond spread proxies for financial turbulence and has strong predictive power for real outcomes during periods of financial distress.	11	1
201509	854	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Since the beginning of this year, the Baa spread has increased about 75 basis points.	11	1
201509	855	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	In the alternative scenario, we assume that it goes up in the fourth quarter by a further 200 basis points relative to baseline and then gradually returns to a more normal level.	11	1
201509	856	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Real GDP contracts sharply almost immediately, and as you can see in panel 6, the unemployment rate— the blue dashed line—rises as much as ¾ percentage point above its baseline trajectory, the black line.	11	1
201509	857	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	As severe as these results are, they could have been worse.	11	1
201509	858	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The funds rate in the alternative scenario runs about 100 basis points below baseline, a policy response that prevents the fallout from being even more serious.	11	1
201509	859	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	This simulation helped inform our assessment that the risks to our forecast for real GDP are weighted to the downside and, especially in light of the adjustments we made to the baseline, that the risks to our unemployment projection are now weighted to the upside.	11	1
201509	860	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Finally, I have updated the “Lockhart dashboard” that I first showed you in July.	11	1
201509	861	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	This exhibit, which is the last page in your packet, summarizes a few of the key pieces of information that will be available to you at the next couple of FOMC meetings.	11	1
201509	862	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Specifically, the data that will first be available at the October meeting are in the gold-shaded region, and the additional observations that will become available in time for the December meeting are shaded in red.	11	1
201509	863	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	(The data that are newly available for today’s meeting are shaded in blue.) September Tealbook projections regarding these variables are shown in regular font, while our forecasts from the July Tealbook are shown in italics.	11	1
201509	864	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	A new memo item at the bottom of the exhibit gives the revisions to equity prices and the foreign exchange value of the dollar since July, as those were two of the key drivers of the revision to our assessment of the outlook.	11	1
201509	865	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	As in July, we expect that inflation will continue to run at a low level through the end of this year.	11	1
201509	866	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	At the time of your December meeting, the latest reading on PCE prices that you will have in hand will be the one for October.	11	1
201509	867	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	We now forecast that topline prices over the three months ending in October will decline at an annual rate of nearly ¾ percent.	11	1
201509	868	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Over the 12 months ending in October—the next pair of lines down—we expect that topline prices will have been unchanged.	11	1
201509	869	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Core inflation is expected to run below 1½ percent through this period, whether measured on a 3-month or 12-month basis.	11	1
201509	870	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	As for the labor market, we have revised down our forecast for the unemployment rate and now expect that you will have a 5 percent print in hand at the time of the December meeting.	11	1
201509	871	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	We also expect to see continued solid payroll job gains.	11	1
201509	872	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The much bigger jobs number that shows up in the September column in this display incorporates both the gain of 210,000 that we expect to be reported for September itself, as well as the upward revision that we expect to be applied to the August number.	11	1
201509	873	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	As I mentioned earlier, we have nudged up our forecast of third-quarter real GDP growth from the 1.9 percent figure shown in the exhibit to around 2¼ percent.	11	1

201509	875	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Thank you, David.	11	1
201509	876	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	I will be referring to the material titled “The International Outlook.”	11	1
201509	877	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Since your previous meeting, developments in China triggered fears of a global economic slowdown and led to widespread turbulence in markets.	11	1
201509	878	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Turning points in the global business cycle are notoriously difficult to forecast, and though we have seen a few in recent decades, we have not predicted any of them.	11	1
201509	879	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Bearing that in mind, even after a very rocky month and a half, we are still projecting a strengthening of foreign growth over the next few quarters.	11	1
201509	880	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	However, as indicated in panel 1 of your first exhibit, based on data that came in over the past month and a half, we now estimate that aggregate foreign GDP growth, which was already quite weak in the first quarter, dropped further, to only 1 percent in the second, the slowest pace since 2009.	11	1
201509	881	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Furthermore, weak incoming data for the third quarter, along with the turbulence in global financial and commodity markets, led us to write down a notably lower path going forward.	11	1
201509	882	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, although we believe the financial market responses to events in China were probably overblown, we agree that downside risks have increased to a material degree.	11	1
201509	883	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	The developments in China that Simon reviewed earlier have raised two inter- related concerns with investors.	11	1
201509	884	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	The first is that China’s economy is not only slowing from the double-digit growth rates of earlier years, but may be falling into something akin to an actual recession.	11	1
201509	885	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	As indicated by the solid red line in panel 2, we do see Chinese growth coming down from its transitory surge in the second quarter, but we are looking for growth to flatten out at around 6 percent, not fall precipitously further.	11	1
201509	886	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Still-strong retail sales suggest that the Chinese economy retains sources of strength, and signs of recovery in the property market are somewhat encouraging.	11	1
201509	887	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Nevertheless, weak incoming data, concerns over the management of economic policy, and our sense that the authorities now face a more difficult task rebalancing the economy in the context of financial vulnerabilities have led us to revise down our forecast from the July Tealbook, the red dashed line.	11	1
201509	888	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	All that said, we are unconvinced by arguments that actual Chinese growth has fallen well below the pace indicated by the official GDP statistics.	11	1
201509	889	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	The blue line in panel 2 shows the results of our nowcasting model, which uses data on industrial production, imports, and retail sales to estimate contemporaneous GDP growth.	11	1
201509	890	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Smoothing through the wiggles, the nowcasting model has continued to track the trend in the official GDP statistics reasonably well this year—again suggesting that growth has declined but not collapsed.	11	1
201509	891	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Besides prospects of a Chinese recession, a second and highly related concern for investors has been that August’s 3 percent devaluation of the RMB would be followed up by substantial further depreciation.	11	1
201509	892	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Certainly, the prospect of the world’s second-largest economy allowing its currency to drop precipitously at a time of fragile global demand would be cause for worry.	11	1
201509	893	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	But barring extreme circumstances, a very large further depreciation of the RMB seems unlikely.	11	1
201509	894	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	At present, China’s authorities appear to be walking a tightrope between their longer-term strategy of increasing the role of market forces in determining the exchange rate and avoiding large, abrupt movements that could destabilize financial markets.	11	1
201509	895	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	As indicated in panel 3, our sense is that, in response to further capital outflows engendered by ongoing concerns about either the economy or future exchange-market policy, the authorities will allow the RMB to slide another couple of percent against the dollar.	11	1
201509	896	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Somewhat further down the road, assuming growth stabilizes and worries of a hard landing subside, we anticipate upward pressures on the renminbi will resume.	11	1
201509	897	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	As Simon has described, the recent developments in China led to especially sharp downdrafts in global markets because many economies, especially in emerging markets, were already struggling with disappointing growth, pronounced vulnerabilities, and anticipations of monetary policy tightening in the United States.	11	1
201509	898	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	These market downdrafts, in turn, will likely put additional pressures on global growth over the near term.	11	1
201509	899	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 4, oil prices took another sharp notch down during the intermeeting period.	11	1
201509	900	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Although most of the declines in oil prices since mid-2014 appear attributable to increased oil supplies, the downturn in August appears to owe mainly to concerns about slowing in China—which accounts for 11 percent of global oil demand—and its knock-on effects on other economies.	11	1
201509	901	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	To be sure, we continue to view declines in oil prices as an eventual plus for the global economy.	11	1
201509	902	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	But our econometric analysis, as well as recent experience, suggests that, in the near term, lower oil prices can be a drag on global growth, as their decline may restrain spending in oil exporters more than it boosts spending in oil importers.	11	1
201509	903	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Besides declines in oil prices, various other market movements have affected the outlook, including widespread declines in equity prices, increases in credit spreads, and, as shown in panel 5, a further appreciation of the dollar.	11	1
201509	904	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	The modest devaluation of the RMB by itself added only about ½ percent to the dollar’s value, but sympathetic depreciations of other Asian currencies, hits to so-called commodity currencies, and general gloom about EME prospects, taken together, led the dollar to appreciate about 2 percent in total.	11	1
201509	905	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	We see the dollar rising a little higher during the rest of the year, reflecting our projection of some further depreciation of the RMB as well as the assumed tightening of Federal Reserve policy, before the dollar flattens out and eventually gives back some of its gains.	11	1
201509	906	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 6, the higher path of the dollar implies that net exports are a source of a bit more drag on the economy than they were in the July Tealbook.	11	1
201509	907	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	In light of developments in China and other emerging markets, the downside risks to the global outlook appear to have increased.	11	1
201509	908	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Your next exhibit presents three inter- related scenarios to examine the effects of a crisis in China that lowers Chinese GDP 7 percent below its baseline path and leads to a 10 percent devaluation of the renminbi against the dollar.	11	1
201509	909	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	The first scenario, which is represented by the green lines in panels 2 through 5, illustrates the direct effect of such a crisis on the US economy, excluding any indirect effect that a China crisis might exert via spillovers to China’s trading partners.	11	1
201509	910	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Turning to panel 3, because China is not a dominant destination for US exports, the direct effects of this shock—again, the green line— lower US GDP only a little below its baseline path—the black line.	11	1
201509	911	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Similarly, headline inflation (panel 4) and the federal funds rate (panel 5) are only slightly restrained.	11	1
201509	912	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	All told, this scenario illustrates that a hard landing in China will lead to significant damage to the US economy only to the extent that it induces broader economic and financial disruptions around the world.	11	1
201509	913	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	The second scenario is labeled “EME slowdown.”	11	1
201509	914	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	In this scenario, turning to the blue line in panel 2, we assume that the China crisis described in the first scenario spills over to other EMEs to an extent consistent with past historical correlations, so that aggregate EME GDP growth falls to zero.	11	1
201509	915	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	However, we assume no financial spillovers to advanced economies, and effects on US growth, inflation, and interest rates, while quite noticeable, are hardly eye-popping.	11	1
201509	916	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	To get eye-popping, our third scenario—represented by the red lines in the panels—embeds the assumption that the recession in China generates much sharper disruptions in other EMEs, along the lines of the distress associated with the Asian and Russian crises of the late 1990s.	11	1
201509	917	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Aggregate EME GDP growth (panel 2) falls below zero and EME currencies decline more than 20 percent against the dollar.	11	1
201509	918	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	We also assume that the turbulence in emerging markets spills over to financial markets in the United States and other advanced economies, triggering sharp declines in equity prices and a widening of credit spreads.	11	1
201509	919	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	The US economy falls into recession and deflation, and the federal funds rate falls back to the zero lower bound.	11	1
201509	920	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	But taking into account the assumptions required to achieve this result, we view the likelihood of this risk materializing as fairly remote.	11	1
201509	921	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	If I could make one final point without sounding like a complete worrywart, I would note that although the global financial turbulence of the past month was triggered by developments in China, anticipation of FOMC liftoff may have played some role in making markets a little more skittish and thus more responsive to Chinese events than they otherwise might have been.	11	1
201509	922	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	Our anticipation is that when you decide to start tightening, volatility in emerging markets will likely remain contained, but scenarios 2 and 3 in this exhibit provide some sense of the tail-risks involved should investor concerns about EME vulnerabilities and the global outlook lead markets to react much more strongly to US monetary tightening that we currently expect.	11	1
201509	923	2015-09-17	meeting	KAMIN	That concludes my remarks, and I’ll pass it on to Francisco.	11	1

201509	954	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	Eleven of you also revised down your projection of the longer-run nominal federal funds rate, typically by 25 basis points.	11	1
201509	955	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	A majority of you project that, at the end of 2018, the appropriate level of the federal funds rate will be close to, albeit still below, your individual judgment of its longer-run level.	11	1
201509	956	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	As in June, almost all of you project levels of the federal funds rate over the next couple of years that are below the prescriptions of a non-inertial Taylor 1999 rule given your projections of core inflation, unemployment gap, and longer-run nominal federal funds rate, indicating that you do not see the Taylor rule as likely to prescribe appropriate policy for the next few years.	11	1
201509	957	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	The medians of these Taylor rule prescriptions, plotted as red diamonds, have shifted up in 2015 and 2016 since June, primarily reflecting the rule’s response to the downward revision in your unemployment rate projections, but have edged down in 2017.	11	1
201509	958	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	For 2015 through 2017, the gap between your projections and the rule’s prescriptions, given your individual forecasts of unemployment and inflation, has widened since June, on average.	11	1
201509	959	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	For 2018, the discrepancy between your federal fund rate projections and Taylor-rule-implied rates narrows considerably as most of you project that the dual mandate can be achieved with the federal funds rate being close to its longer-term normal level.	11	1
201509	960	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	The final exhibit shows your assessments of the uncertainty and risks surrounding your economic projections.	11	1
201509	961	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	As shown in the figures to the left, your views regarding uncertainty have not changed in a material way.	11	1
201509	962	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	Most of you continue to judge the level of uncertainty about your individual projections of GDP growth, the unemployment rate, and inflation as broadly similar to the average level over the past 20 years.	11	1
201509	963	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	As shown in the panels to the right, most of you continue to see the risks to real GDP growth and the unemployment rate as broadly balanced, though seven of you now view risks to GDP growth as weighted to the downside—three more than in June—and four more of you now see the risks to unemployment as weighted to the upside.	11	1
201509	964	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	The downside risks to GDP growth that you cited include a weaker outlook abroad and tighter financial conditions than currently embedded in your forecasts.	11	1
201509	965	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	As reported in the third and fourth panels on the right, nine of you now see risks to inflation as weighted to the downside—four more than in June.	11	1
201509	966	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	Recent declines in market-based measures of inflation compensation and commodity prices and the appreciation of the dollar were noted as factors that could place greater downward pressure on prices than currently embedded in your forecasts.	11	1
201509	967	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	Thank you.	11	1
201509	968	2015-09-17	meeting	COVAS	That concludes the presentation.	11	1

201509	976	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If the staff were asked to talk about scenarios that might give rise to an overrun in inflation, what would that potentially look like?	12	1
201509	977	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	We actually contemplated putting in one of those.	12	1
201509	978	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The one that I think is plausible for us is that there’s some drift that occurs in inflation expectations.	12	1
201509	979	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	We debated whether the more plausible direction of drift in inflation expectations is up or down.	12	1
201509	980	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	But I do think that an upward drift of inflation expectations is certainly within our confidence intervals.	12	1
201509	981	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	At the moment, the more natural mechanism, it seems to me, is that the little bit of extra transitory restraint that’s in the inflation pipeline from the dollar and the oil prices is going to put a little more gravitational pull downward on inflation.	12	1
201509	982	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	And so my own assessment is that while I see inflation expectations drift in either direction as quite plausible, I think it’s a little more likely downward.	12	1
201509	983	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	But if I were to put my finger on one scenario that could provide for some upward lift on inflation, I’d point to that one, importantly out of our collective professional ignorance about the basic mechanisms that form inflation expectations.	12	1

201509	986	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	12	1
201509	987	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	David, let me pick up where you left off there, and thanks for panel 3 on output gap estimates, which makes my question a little more relevant because you mentioned the FRB/US model.	12	1
201509	988	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	When I was looking through Tealbook A, on page 79, I came across alternative models and the FRB/US model.	12	1
201509	989	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I noticed that the core PCE projection coming out of the FRB/US model has 2017 inflation moving down to 1.0 percent, whereas in the June Tealbook it’s at 1.5 percent.	12	1
201509	990	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I wonder what features of the data and the model are generating that somewhat aberrant behavior.	12	1
201509	991	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The FRB/US model has a different wage-price mechanism than the judgmental forecast does.	12	1
201509	992	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The model pays attention to compensation trends.	12	1
201509	993	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	There’s an equation for price markup over marginal cost in the FRB/US model.	12	1
201509	994	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	I’m going to look here for confirmation from my former FRB/US colleague.	12	1
201509	995	2015-09-17	meeting	REIFSCHNEIDER	That’s correct.	12	1
201509	996	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	I don’t think we provide you with a graph of the markup of price over marginal cost in your Tealbook materials, but in putting together our inflation projection, the staff has pretty much written that relationship off as noninformative.	12	1
201509	997	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The FRB/US model, partly for a bit of intellectual diversity, hasn’t chucked that specification overboard and views the high level of prices over marginal costs as posing a downside impetus on inflation.	12	1
201509	998	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	And so that’s mainly what’s generating this difference.	12	1
201509	999	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	So the forecast was already pretty low in the June Tealbook at 1½ percent for 2017, but the differential data coming in seem to have moved it downward.	12	1
201509	1000	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Yes.	12	1
201509	1001	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	My guess is that two things are going on there.	12	1
201509	1002	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	One—probably the more material of the two—is the recent tranche of disappointing compensation news that we got.	12	1
201509	1003	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	The other—which I suspect is quantitatively tiny, but might be there in principle—is that there was a tiny upward revision in nonmarket prices in the annual revision.	12	1
201509	1004	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	So the FRB/US model might be picking up on that, but I’m guessing that the larger of those two is the compensation.	12	1
201509	1005	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Just to close this out, is it fair to say that this implementation of the FRB/US model is putting less weight on the longer-term inflation expectations anchor than other analyses that we normally are looking at or the preferred inflation model that you’re using?	12	1
201509	1006	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	I think so.	12	1
201509	1007	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	There’s an inflation objective for policymakers in the FRB/US model, and that has complete credibility.	12	1
201509	1008	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	So households and businesses don’t question the 2 percent objective.	12	1
201509	1009	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I’m sorry.	12	1
201509	1010	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Let me clarify.	12	1
201509	1011	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Yes, it has that feature in there, but that’s not enough to pull up the inflation forecast given the other countervailing data developments.	12	1
201509	1012	2015-09-17	meeting	WILCOX	Yes, that’s evident in the projection that you’re pointing to.	12	1

201509	1022	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We’ll start our go-round with President Rosengren.	13	1
201509	1023	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1024	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Since our previous meeting, we have seen further improvement in labor markets, although the recent data on wages and prices are consistent with the continued persistent undershooting of our 2 percent inflation goal.	13	1
201509	1025	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Earlier evidence of accelerating compensation in both average hourly earnings and the employment cost index has been revised away, resulting in almost all wage measures continuing to rise at a surprisingly steady 2 percent.	13	1
201509	1026	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because both aggregated and disaggregated data on wages and prices continue to come in quite low, my own forecast does not expect us to reach our inflation target within two years.	13	1
201509	1027	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	This is qualitatively consistent with the staff forecast of inflation in the Tealbook.	13	1
201509	1028	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because wages and prices have not responded to much-improved labor market conditions in aggregate or, really, even in the disaggregated data, I have lowered my estimate of the longer- run unemployment rate to 4.8 percent.	13	1
201509	1029	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition to the evidence from wages and prices, this estimate of the longer-run unemployment rate is consistent with the rising share of the workforce that is more highly educated and older, demographic groups that historically have had lower unemployment rates.	13	1
201509	1030	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, the most pertinent data for this meeting are probably not the government data releases on wages, prices, and real activity, but rather the financial data that have been unusually turbulent since August 24.	13	1
201509	1031	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Stock markets in many parts of the world are down 5 to 10 percent, with some emerging markets down appreciably more in dollar terms.	13	1
201509	1032	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, volatility has risen significantly not only because of the sharp stock price declines, but also because of rising interday and daily volatility.	13	1
201509	1033	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	During periods of significant financial turbulence the FOMC has tended to follow easier policy, a point that will be made in a Boston Fed paper to be presented at our October conference on financial stability.	13	1
201509	1034	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	After Black Monday in October 1987, the FOMC had daily calls through the end of that month to monitor financial and economic conditions and lowered interest rates.	13	1
201509	1035	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Recent stock price movements have been much more modest.	13	1
201509	1036	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	On Black Monday, the stock market fell 22 percent, whereas on August 24, the Dow opened with a decline of over 1,000 points, or about 6 percent, but ended the day down a bit over 3½ percent.	13	1
201509	1037	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Nonetheless, the stock price declines did receive significant attention.	13	1
201509	1038	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is certainly possible that some of the eye-catching declines have more to do with problems related to financial market structure rather than a change in the economic outlook.	13	1
201509	1039	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	On August 24, with the Shanghai index down a little over 8 percent, the New York Stock Exchange imposed Rule 48, which allows market makers to not post prices prior to opening.	13	1
201509	1040	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Along with a 1,000 point drop at the opening, a large number of individual stocks, ETFs, and other exchange- traded securities hit circuit breakers, with trading halted over 1,200 times across 466 securities, with 300 of the securities being ETFs.	13	1
201509	1041	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, the prices of a surprising number of large ETFs declined dramatically, with 188 declining in excess of 30 percent.	13	1
201509	1042	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Some ETFs declined by more than 50 percent.	13	1
201509	1043	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In some instances, two ETFs with similar strategies experienced materially different interday price movements.	13	1
201509	1044	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Further, the affected securities spanned different sectors and sizes—that is, they were not singularly focused.	13	1
201509	1045	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	This, again, speaks to potential fragilities in the financial market structure.	13	1
201509	1046	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It’s quite possible that Rule 48 and circuit breakers in individual stocks complicated normal ETF arbitrage, leading to unusually large temporary declines.	13	1
201509	1047	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Ironically, the circuit breakers were implemented in response to May 2010’s flash crash in which the Dow experienced an interday decline of over 1,000 points.	13	1
201509	1048	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In a manner similar to August 24’s events, many stocks and ETFs experienced sharp price declines that reversed within a short period.	13	1
201509	1049	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If problems with market mechanics explain much of the recent volatility in financial markets, we have some significant financial stability analysis that needs to be done to better understand both the role of market mechanics and, possibly, regulatory policy solutions.	13	1
201509	1050	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	But, for now, the appropriate response to this financial upheaval is to reflect the realized loss of wealth and exchange rate movements in our model equations and assume the additional economic information content is modest.	13	1
201509	1051	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Of course, there is some risk in doing so, as it is not yet clear how persistent asset price movements will be and, generally speaking, households and firms tend to respond to such price movements only when they persist for some time.	13	1
201509	1052	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In any event, this is roughly how we folded the events into our own baseline forecast.	13	1
201509	1053	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, there is a darker potential story.	13	1
201509	1054	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Our models do a poor job of integrating financial market information, something that David mentioned and something we were all too aware of in 2008.	13	1
201509	1055	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is possible that financial markets are reflecting weaker global growth or other more-fundamental problems that we do not fully understand.	13	1
201509	1056	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In this case, my modal forecast is too optimistic, and the downside risk should be significantly elevated.	13	1
201509	1057	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Unfortunately, I do not think we have enough time to fully process recent market turbulence.	13	1
201509	1058	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We certainly do not want to begin our first tightening amid a global slowdown.	13	1
201509	1059	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I can also imagine the difficulty of keeping the reverse repo facility small during a period of very elevated market turbulence, as many might flock to this convenient source of safe short-term financing during a time of financial tumult.	13	1
201509	1060	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Although my baseline forecast involves the assumption of relatively modest effects from the recent financial turbulence, with magnitudes similar to those of the Tealbook, I think it would be wise to wait for more data that can validate the assumption of modest disruption before taking action based on that assumption.	13	1
201509	1061	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I will discuss this in more detail tomorrow.	13	1
201509	1062	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1063	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201509	1064	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	13	1
201509	1065	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1066	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	My remarks today will be centered on what has changed and not changed with respect to the national economic outlook since our previous meeting.	13	1
201509	1067	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	My view is that the general contours of the national outlook have not changed very much during the intermeeting period, and that we are on the precipice of making a decision that will demonstrate excessive sensitivity of the Committee to short-term movements in financial markets, especially equity markets.	13	1
201509	1068	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Historically, the Committee has not wanted to react directly to equity price movements, as they are far too unpredictable over short periods and are as likely as not to reverse themselves over the medium term.	13	1
201509	1069	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	If the Committee is changing its view on this issue, we should say so as forthrightly as possible and inform private-sector players about how we plan to proceed when future movements in equity market prices present themselves, either up or down, in future meetings of this Committee.	13	1
201509	1070	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	One way to get a handle on the intermeeting financial market turmoil is to consider so- called financial conditions indexes or the closely related financial stress indexes.	13	1
201509	1071	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	A 2012 Federal Reserve Bank of St Louis Review article by Kevin Kliesen, Michael Owyang, and Katarina Vermann documents the similarities and differences between a wide variety of such indexes.	13	1
201509	1072	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Of course, we have a favorite, which is the St Louis Fed financial stress index, and it has indeed risen sharply over the intermeeting period.	13	1
201509	1073	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Still, the level of the index remains well below the levels reached during the height of the European sovereign debt crisis in 2011 and 2012, not to mention far below the levels reached in 2008 and 2009.	13	1
201509	1074	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In addition, the index was arguably abnormally low during recent quarters and years, with volatility at low ebb and some interest rate spreads unusually compressed.	13	1
201509	1075	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	From this point of view, one might welcome at least some of the return to a more normal market operation.	13	1
201509	1076	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In short, the increase in the St Louis Fed’s financial stress index, or other related indexes, is not enough to cause me to make sufficient revisions to my forecast that would alter my path for monetary policy.	13	1
201509	1077	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I understand that many may be worried about a weaker growth outlook globally than would have been projected at the previous FOMC meeting, but my view is that many of the weak spots globally were clearly flagged during June and July, and that marginally weaker growth prospects globally are unlikely to have a meaningful effect on US growth prospects.	13	1
201509	1078	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Accordingly, we have continued to project in St Louis above-trend growth for the second half of 2015 and, indeed, over the forecast horizon.	13	1
201509	1079	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	We think our growth call for the remainder of 2015 is close to the September 10 Blue Chip forecast, which itself is notably above the Board staff view.	13	1
201509	1080	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Although it is always good to be cautious, we think, on the basis of the data available today, that the staff view is overly pessimistic concerning near-term growth.	13	1
201509	1081	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In addition, the Committee has now received information on the revisions to first-half real GDP growth, which now appears to have been above trend, adding to the picture of an economy that continues to push forward even in the face of a large dollar appreciation over the past year or more.	13	1
201509	1082	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Above-trend growth is likely to continue to mean even tighter labor markets.	13	1
201509	1083	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Jobs reports since the previous meeting have generally been very good.	13	1
201509	1084	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	And, if recent history is a guide, I would expect more upward revisions to currently reported jobs numbers as we go forward.	13	1
201509	1085	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The staff noted this as well.	13	1
201509	1086	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Unemployment insurance claims per person in the labor force is at a multidecade low.	13	1
201509	1087	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Job openings per unemployed worker is exceptionally high, and the unemployment rate itself fell to 5.1 percent in the latest reading, matching what the staff projected at the previous meeting would only happen two and a half years from now, at the end of 2017.	13	1
201509	1088	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I appreciate that the staff has now added some downward tilt to its unemployment projections, which have consistently been too pessimistic over the past several years.	13	1
201509	1089	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Still, it is probably not enough, as the unemployment rate is likely to fall below 4½ percent over the forecast horizon with above-trend growth and no major negative shocks.	13	1
201509	1090	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I think these outcomes are already in train, as the Committee has already committed to a very easy monetary policy during this coming phase of the business cycle.	13	1
201509	1091	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	There has, of course, been considerable talk about Chinese growth prospects during the intermeeting period.	13	1
201509	1092	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	My assessment is as follows.	13	1
201509	1093	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The Shanghai composite index is not a meaningful indicator of US growth prospects and probably not of China’s growth prospects either.	13	1
201509	1094	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	This index rose from around 2,000 in the first half of 2014 to 5,000 by June of 2015 before falling to around 3,000 during the intermeeting period.	13	1
201509	1095	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	This was a bubble that burst because of factors specific to China.	13	1
201509	1096	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I take the signal for the United States to be small or zero.	13	1
201509	1097	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Of course, many have commented that China may be growing slower than the official numbers indicate.	13	1
201509	1098	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I have, in fact, flagged this comment from business contacts with significant operations in Chinese markets in past meetings, especially those in the energy and manufacturing sectors.	13	1
201509	1099	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I do think that growth may be somewhat slower than official data suggest, but I do not think this is news compared with what was known at our previous meeting.	13	1
201509	1100	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	It is an old issue.	13	1
201509	1101	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	And, in my view, there is scant evidence at this point that China is entering a true hard landing, and on this point I agree with the Board staff analysis.	13	1
201509	1102	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	That brings us to US equity prices, which are down approximately 7 percent during the intermeeting period as of the Tealbook publication.	13	1
201509	1103	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	This is news, and, indeed, this is why I am concerned that our pending action will be viewed as a reaction to this development.	13	1
201509	1104	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	One thought that I alluded to earlier is that this may be a more appropriate valuation than previously.	13	1
201509	1105	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	We should think of an appropriate level of equity prices relative to potential GDP, and we should expect equity valuations—really, the value of the US corporate sector—to return to this appropriate level regardless of week-to-week volatility.	13	1
201509	1106	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	If that’s the view, then temporary movements in equity valuations would not have an effect on macroeconomic forecasts and, therefore, on monetary policy.	13	1
201509	1107	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	My final comments concern inflation, which is running low today but is likely to strengthen over the forecast horizon.	13	1
201509	1108	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	According to my board of directors, the firms represented there all expect wages to increase 3 percent this year, even firms that have workers that are on the lower end of the income distribution.	13	1
201509	1109	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I was surprised by that.	13	1
201509	1110	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Low oil prices are having a large effect on inflation, but this effect will dissipate going forward.	13	1
201509	1111	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In any event, low oil prices are ultimately a bullish factor for the US economy, not a negative factor.	13	1
201509	1112	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	TIPS-based expected inflation measures are low and have fallen during the intermeeting period.	13	1
201509	1113	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I would normally be quite concerned about this, but these measures are unfortunately highly conflated with oil price movements and so are difficult to read in the current circumstances.	13	1
201509	1114	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Overall, I am very concerned that the Committee does not overreact to what are essentially financial market developments as opposed to real-side developments during the intermeeting period.	13	1
201509	1115	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I see very tight labor markets ahead, barring a large shock.	13	1

201509	1124	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	As we saw when it dipped earlier this year, the index is at odds with the generally upbeat assessment by our contacts, who indicated that activity remains moderately strong despite less-favorable exchange rates and softer growth in emerging market economies.	13	1

201509	1130	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Fifth District housing markets continue to strengthen despite supply constraints on the building side that were said to be holding back activity.	13	1

201509	1132	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The time required to go from initiation to completion of a single-family home is said to have increased.	13	1

201509	1134	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Spec building is increasing at price points around $1 million, and we have heard several contacts use the term “bubble” in connection with the multifamily sector.	13	1
201509	1135	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	That said, vacancy rates remain low, and I am never quite sure what people mean by the word “bubble.”	13	1
201509	1136	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Contacts generally reported that commercial real estate and building activity were robust in many regions within our District.	13	1
201509	1137	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Some markets have seen a surge in hotel construction and the emergence of spec office construction.	13	1
201509	1138	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Reports of labor shortages and difficulty finding qualified workers continue to proliferate.	13	1
201509	1139	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Contacts say the number of unfilled job openings is rising, as is the time it takes to fill openings.	13	1
201509	1140	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Employers are converting temporary workers to permanent status more rapidly to avoid losing them, and they are making more initial hires on a permanent basis rather than a temporary one.	13	1
201509	1141	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Although labor scarcity is not universal across occupations, it appears to go well beyond IT and skilled trades.	13	1
201509	1142	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Many contacts cite shortages for lower-wage jobs, such as those in the hospitality and retail sectors.	13	1
201509	1143	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I continue to hear widespread reports of wage pressures in the Fifth District.	13	1
201509	1144	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I recognize that the second-quarter ECI number appears to have thrown cold water on the notion of nominal wage acceleration in the national data.	13	1
201509	1145	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Nevertheless, our contacts report that wage pressures are resulting in some outsized wage gains, and they suggest that such pressures are prevalent in a broadening array of industries and occupations.	13	1
201509	1146	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Additionally, the wage components of our manufacturing and service-sector surveys have strengthened considerably over the past year or so and are now quite close to historic highs.	13	1
201509	1147	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Perhaps the gains we hear about are being offset by weaker wage gains in other occupations, but our reports do seem to indicate that a broader portion of the labor market has tightened in recent months.	13	1
201509	1148	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Despite these indications of rising labor costs, there are no new reports of broad-based acceleration in prices and inflation expectations, at least as evidenced by our survey results, and contact reports suggest that expectations appear to be well anchored.	13	1
201509	1149	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Turning to the national picture, the most notable aspect of recent economic performance, in my view, besides the unexpectedly rapid tightening in labor markets, is the behavior of household expenditures.	13	1
201509	1150	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Real consumer spending accelerated from less than 2 percent in the years prior to 2014 to over 3 percent since.	13	1
201509	1151	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	This faster pace was interrupted in the first quarter of this year by what are now known to have been temporary factors, including unusually harsh winter weather.	13	1
201509	1152	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	But with that pothole behind us, consumption growth has returned to a 3 percent annual rate.	13	1
201509	1153	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Reflecting the momentum in labor markets, real income growth is likely to continue at a solid pace.	13	1
201509	1154	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I expect real PCE growth to remain in the 2½ to 3 percent range, distinctly higher than the average from 2010 through 2014.	13	1
201509	1155	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	This sustained step-up in the pace of consumption growth is important to my thinking about interest rates.	13	1
201509	1156	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I’ll say more about this later, but, broadly speaking, higher real consumption growth should be associated with higher real interest rates.	13	1
201509	1157	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Other components of GDP are showing reasonably healthy growth as well.	13	1
201509	1158	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Business fixed investment weakened beginning late last year, but recent reports indicate that capital goods orders bottomed out last spring and have been increasing since.	13	1
201509	1159	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Nonresidential construction spending, apart from oil and gas, has registered strong gains as well, as has residential investment spending.	13	1
201509	1160	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Even before the August employment report, I would have argued that we had seen substantial further improvements in labor market conditions this year.	13	1
201509	1161	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	With monthly job gains averaging over 200,000 per month and growth in the prime working-age population having slowed considerably, it is not surprising that the unemployment rate has continued to decline at an impressive rate.	13	1
201509	1162	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The August employment report obviously revealed additional labor market improvement.	13	1
201509	1163	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I have spoken in past meetings about broader measures of labor utilization.	13	1
201509	1164	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I have also spoken about alternative approaches to calculating an appropriate benchmark to gauge labor market conditions.	13	1
201509	1165	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	At this point, however, it seems clear that virtually all measures of labor market utilization have fallen enough to be statistically indistinguishable from any plausible normative benchmark one might choose to represent maximum employment.	13	1
201509	1166	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	As a result, I don’t see how we can say we have not seen further improvement in labor markets.	13	1
201509	1167	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Some argue that there is likely to be additional slack in labor markets if nominal wage rates are not accelerating.	13	1
201509	1168	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	But real wage rates are related to productivity growth, and productivity growth has been slow for several years now.	13	1
201509	1169	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Wage growth in real terms has at least kept pace with productivity gains over that time period and, in the past year, has significantly outpaced productivity.	13	1
201509	1170	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	So I don’t see the behavior of wage rates as providing evidence that there is any remaining labor market slack.	13	1
201509	1171	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The JOLTS data also seem to suggest that labor market slack is minimal.	13	1
201509	1172	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Job openings have been increasing more rapidly than hiring for several years now, but the divergence has widened at an increasing pace this year.	13	1
201509	1173	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	As of July, job openings have increased by 12½ percent from their average in the fourth quarter of 2014, while the hiring rate has been virtually flat.	13	1
201509	1174	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The natural interpretation would seem to be that employers are having an increasingly hard time finding suitable workers to hire, and slack in any meaningful sense has been substantially reduced.	13	1
201509	1175	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	A solid economic outlook and the relative stability of inflation expectations, I think, should give us confidence that inflation will return to 2 percent once the temporary effect of the recent fall in oil prices and strengthening of the dollar have dissipated.	13	1
201509	1176	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The behavior of inflation following the previous oil and dollar moves should bolster that confidence.	13	1
201509	1177	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Over the past six months—that is, from January, which is when energy prices bottomed out, to July, which is the latest month for which we have this data—headline PCE inflation has averaged 2.2 percent, while core PCE inflation has averaged 1.7 percent.	13	1
201509	1178	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	One might argue that the strength in headline inflation was aided by the 7.8 percent rebound in energy prices from January to July, but core inflation was relatively close to 2 percent despite the continuing decrease in import prices this year.	13	1
201509	1179	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I think our experience following the previous disinflationary surprise is good evidence that the 1½ percent decline in the overall price level over the six months prior to last January was transitory and left no lasting effect on trend inflation.	13	1
201509	1180	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Thus, to the extent that the current disinflationary impulse from energy prices and the dollar resembles the previous one, it ought to bolster our confidence that inflation will rebound to 2 percent as it did earlier this year.	13	1
201509	1181	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Recent financial market volatility both here and abroad has captured popular attention and seems to have shaped a great deal of market commentary about our pending policy decision.	13	1
201509	1182	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	For me, it’s hard to discern meaningful implications for US growth prospects or inflation trends, and it hasn’t had a significant effect on my policy views.	13	1
201509	1183	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	These recent events bring to mind several historical instances—President Rosengren cited one or two—in which large stock market declines have occurred in the midst of extended economic expansions.	13	1
201509	1184	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The years 1966, 1987, and 1998 stand out.	13	1
201509	1185	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	In each of these instances, it is clear with hindsight that stock market gyrations did not signal a deflection in the trajectory of US economic activity, and, in fact, in each case the economy continued to expand.	13	1
201509	1186	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I also think it’s clear with hindsight that our policy reactions were too accommodative.	13	1
201509	1187	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	For example, in the fall of 1998, we cut interest rates three times following financial market reactions to the emerging market turmoil and, as a result, fell behind the curve in 1999.	13	1
201509	1188	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I think the lesson is that we should be careful to not overreact to financial market volatility that is not demonstrably connected to weaker economic fundamentals.	13	1
201509	1189	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201509	1223	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	The labor market has made significant progress.	13	1

201509	1253	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	In the historical data, inflation surprises are frequent and large.	13	1

201509	1274	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Firms are increasingly willing to spend on employee training to address skills requirements.	13	1
201509	1275	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This was the fifth consecutive cycle of contacts in which we heard comments on growing wage pressures for selected job categories or in selected geographies or both.	13	1
201509	1276	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	It was noteworthy that, this past cycle, the District contacts yielded a more generalized sense of rising wage pressures.	13	1
201509	1277	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Turning to my outlook, my baseline forecast for growth falls in the 2½ to 3 percent range over the next few years, which puts me on a stronger growth path than the current Tealbook.	13	1
201509	1278	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My growth outlook is accompanied by continued absorption of labor market slack, broadly defined, and accelerating measured wage pressure.	13	1
201509	1279	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I continue to have confidence that inflation will move to target in the medium term, but I’m not very optimistic we’ll see much improvement in the inflation trend this year.	13	1
201509	1280	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I expect transitory factors, such as oil and commodity prices, will exert downward pressure on headline and core inflation measures for the next few quarters at least.	13	1
201509	1281	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This view lines up with the Tealbook.	13	1
201509	1282	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The only meaningful change in my assessment of the economy from the July meeting pertains to my sense of the balance of risks.	13	1
201509	1283	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The recent volatility in the markets, apparently a response to increased uncertainty triggered by global economic and financial developments, has not subsided entirely as of this meeting date.	13	1
201509	1284	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	It’s too early to know whether this episode amounts to a bona fide shock or just a nervous spasm in the markets.	13	1
201509	1285	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	It’s also too early to detect any significant effect on the real economy.	13	1
201509	1286	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m not projecting a material effect, but evaluation of that question will require some time.	13	1

201509	1289	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	13	1
201509	1290	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1291	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do have one comment about the Twelfth District economy, specifically the Bay Area economy.	13	1
201509	1292	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I don’t know if you saw this in the news, but our housing crisis is so extreme that the Salesforce conference, which is going on all week in San Francisco—another reason I’m happy to be here and not at home—brought in a luxury cruise ship to provide housing for the people coming to their big conference because the hotels were all booked.	13	1
201509	1293	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	At Airbnb.com, which is very popular in San Francisco, the rates were described as “astronomical.”	13	1
201509	1294	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think, the fact that people are now living on luxury cruise ships gives you a sense of the state of the San Francisco economy.	13	1
201509	1295	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Over the past five years, real GDP growth has averaged a little over 2 percent, and the unemployment rate has fallen nearly 1 percentage point per year.	13	1
201509	1296	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	All indications are that this pace of expansion, both in terms of growth and the labor market, is continuing despite the sizable global headwinds.	13	1
201509	1297	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, my contacts point to a virtuous cycle of job growth and consumer spending across a broad set of regions and sectors, and I see moderate GDP growth combined with a still-subdued pace of productivity growth, implying that the unemployment rate should continue its downward trajectory at least through next year.	13	1
201509	1298	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	This ongoing strengthening of the labor market is in the context of an economy that’s already at or very near full employment.	13	1
201509	1299	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Therefore, my forecast, like that in the Tealbook, implies that the unemployment rate will fall significantly below the natural rate of unemployment next year and remain there for quite some time.	13	1
201509	1300	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, like President Bullard, I see this as already in train, in that the momentum in the economy is already in place to create those circumstances, and it doesn’t depend on any policy decisions we make at this time.	13	1
201509	1301	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	https://Airbnb.com Running such a high-pressure economy arguably has some benefits, at least for a while.	13	1
201509	1302	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	It may speed the processes of squeezing out remaining pockets of labor market weakness and drawing in some of those who are still sitting on the sidelines.	13	1
201509	1303	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	It should also accelerate progress in reaching our 2 percent inflation target.	13	1
201509	1304	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But there are risks as well, especially if this is allowed to go on for too long.	13	1
201509	1305	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The economic pot may move from a healthy simmer to a full boil and eventually boil over.	13	1
201509	1306	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Managing this risk requires that we respect the lags between monetary policy actions and the effects they have on the economy, and that we not allow imbalances to emerge and grow that can ultimately destabilize the economy.	13	1
201509	1307	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The paths to expansion provide a cautionary tale in this regard.	13	1
201509	1308	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In both cases, the unemployment rate drifted lower and lower, falling below the natural rate, and eventually the economy outran its fundamentals and became increasingly fueled by excessive optimism.	13	1
201509	1309	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the end, the high-pressure economy proved unsustainable, collapsing under its own weight, at great social and economic cost—a topic I will return to tomorrow.	13	1
201509	1310	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Of course, managing this risk also requires one to know how far is too far, and that brings me to the question of the natural rate of unemployment.	13	1
201509	1311	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’ve argued in the past that I view the unemployment gap, the gap between the unemployment rate and its natural rate, the long-run equilibrium value, as being a good gauge of overall slack, but that leads us, of course, to think hard about what the natural rate of unemployment is and how to best estimate that.	13	1
201509	1312	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We have spent a lot of time in the Federal Reserve System, and especially the San Francisco Fed, thinking about this issue over the years.	13	1
201509	1313	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And on the heels of the Great Recession, my staff and many others in the System really wrestled with the possibility that the persistent labor market dysfunction related to mismatch or worker scarring might have substantially increased the natural rate, and our conclusion then and now is that the long-run natural rate wasn’t, in fact, much affected by these factors.	13	1
201509	1314	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And now we’re faced with a different question, and that is, with the unemployment rate so low today, we’re asking ourselves whether the natural rate may actually be lower than its pre- recession levels.	13	1
201509	1315	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, of course, a recent analysis by Board staff, as Governor Tarullo commented on at one of our previous meetings, considers this possibility, and that definitely spurred some further research at the Federal Reserve Bank of San Francisco.	13	1
201509	1316	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The Board staff analysis concluded that the secular decline in the labor share of income, which is well documented, has pushed down the natural rate of unemployment as well in recent decades.	13	1
201509	1317	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	They argue that, basically, the decline in the labor share reflects a decline in worker bargaining power which lowers labor costs and makes it more profitable for businesses to hire workers.	13	1
201509	1318	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	With the greater profitability of hiring workers, firms want to go out and create more vacancies in order to take advantage of this opportunity to hire more workers and make more money.	13	1
201509	1319	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In addition, with this increase in job vacancies, it also should be easier for workers to find jobs.	13	1
201509	1320	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	So we should see some signs that job-matching rates are going up.	13	1
201509	1321	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In their paper, they find some evidence for the first hypothesis.	13	1
201509	1322	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	There is a positive correlation between labor share and the ratio of vacancies to unemployed across industries and states.	13	1
201509	1323	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And we found this idea intriguing—in fact, provocative.	13	1
201509	1324	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But after a deeper look at the theory and the evidence, I’m unconvinced.	13	1
201509	1325	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	First, the theoretical implications of a declining labor share for the natural rate of unemployment are far from definitive.	13	1
201509	1326	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Some work by my own staff shows that a decline in labor share doesn’t automatically imply that firms can get higher profits by creating new jobs.	13	1
201509	1327	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	There’s an example they studied, that if financial intermediaries are receiving an increasing share of the surplus from output, businesses and workers are both being squeezed and job creation will fall along with the labor share.	13	1
201509	1328	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	So, in their model, you would find a fall in labor share could actually push up the natural rate of unemployment.	13	1
201509	1329	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, more importantly, the evidence is inconsistent with the theory.	13	1
201509	1330	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Looking at the time series data for the United States, vacancies per unemployed worker have not increased as the labor share has fallen over the previous couple of decades.	13	1
201509	1331	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	If anything, the data show somewhat of a downward rather than upward movement in recent decades.	13	1
201509	1332	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And looking at the worker side of the equation, you see the same thing.	13	1
201509	1333	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The job-finding rates appear to have fallen, not risen, as the theory would suggest, and we’ve looked at this across different subgroups—short-term and long-term unemployed, and people out of the labor force.	13	1
201509	1334	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, the consistent finding is that job-finding rates are not rising the way the theory would suggest.	13	1
201509	1335	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I really don’t see convincing evidence that the natural rate has come down because of a fall in labor share.	13	1
201509	1336	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	With little evidence that the labor market has become more dysfunctional, my staff has gone back to the tried-and-true method of thinking about the natural rate of unemployment, building on some research that was done at the Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago, and that’s to focus on the composition of the labor force.	13	1
201509	1337	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Basically, we’re going back to George Perry’s work from 1970 that said the time needed to find a good job match varies across worker groups, depending on age and other things.	13	1
201509	1338	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Think about young workers—they tend to have less-stable employment patterns than older workers.	13	1
201509	1339	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That translates into higher unemployment rates on average.	13	1
201509	1340	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s an old and well-studied idea in labor markets, and studies differ in how they account for this influence on the overall unemployment rate.	13	1
201509	1341	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	What my staff did is, they looked at the pre- recession average unemployment rate for groups defined by age, gender, education, and race.	13	1
201509	1342	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	They weighted them up by changes in the population shares since 2007, and based on average unemployment rates for the 20 years before the recession, this method yields an estimate of the natural rate prevailing today of 5.0 percent.	13	1
201509	1343	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, the Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago staff did a very similar analysis and used similar methods.	13	1
201509	1344	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	They looked at a shorter period of time, and they got a somewhat lower estimate.	13	1
201509	1345	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, again, going back to this research that we’ve been doing about labor market dynamics and whether there have been structural shifts in the labor market, we’re not really finding any evidence of that.	13	1
201509	1346	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We decided to stick with looking at a 20-year pre-recession sample, and that’s where we came up with the 5 percent number.	13	1
201509	1347	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, I don’t expect demographic factors to actually change much over the next few years.	13	1
201509	1348	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	So that is my long-run view of the labor market.	13	1
201509	1349	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	As I said earlier, I expect the unemployment gap to turn negative later this year and remain so in coming years.	13	1
201509	1350	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	This will push up underlying inflation more quickly toward our target, and that is a good thing.	13	1
201509	1351	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In my forecast, we achieve our 2 percent inflation objective in early 2017 when the effects of the dollar appreciation and of falling oil prices have dissipated—I think this is similar to President Mester’s view.	13	1
201509	1352	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’d just mention, we did spend quite a bit of time with the annual revisions, thinking long and hard about some of our long-run views.	13	1
201509	1353	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And, similarly to President Mester, I did bring down somewhat my estimate of not only the natural rate to 5 percent, but also long-term growth to about 1.9 percent—based on our research on trends, demographics, and productivity—and the real natural rate of interest to 1.5 percent.	13	1
201509	1354	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And for those who like to read all the details or they can’t sleep at night, I am respondent number 6 in the SEP.	13	1
