201509	1415	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1416	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	I am going to start by talking about the outlook for the energy sector.	13	1
201509	1417	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	This will build on some of Steve Kamin’s comments.	13	1
201509	1418	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Oil price uncertainty, as measured by the oil volatility index, is approaching exceptionally high levels, similar to what we saw at the start of this year and in 2011.	13	1
201509	1419	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Our view, informed by discussion with industry contacts, is that there is likely to be more downside than upside risk at current prices.	13	1
201509	1420	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	That is, we believe oil prices may well fall further from here and stay lower for longer than had been previously expected.	13	1
201509	1421	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Let me explain some of the reasons why.	13	1
201509	1422	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	First, on the demand side, a significant issue, which we have all talked about, is a possible further slowing of growth in China and China- linked economies.	13	1
201509	1423	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Second, the summer driving season—which, by the way, was very strong— has ended, and we have yet to enter the peak winter heating season.	13	1
201509	1424	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Third and lastly, refineries are now shutting down for normal scheduled maintenance, and that will go on for the next few months.	13	1
201509	1425	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	On the supply side, inventories of crude are large and growing.	13	1
201509	1426	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Global production is more than 2 million barrels per day above global consumption.	13	1
201509	1427	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	And although rig count has notably declined, this is more than offset, in our view, by a very large shadow inventory of drilled but uncompleted wells that could be brought into production rapidly, depending on oil prices.	13	1
201509	1428	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	We have accumulated this supply overhang even as supply outages outside the United States have restricted world oil production by an estimated 3½ million barrels per day.	13	1
201509	1429	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	If any of these outages are resolved—for example, in Libya or Iran—the additional production could easily offset supply declines expected in the United States in coming months.	13	1
201509	1430	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	In addition, much of the world’s marginal cost production is located in the United States, and, to a much lesser extent, in Canada and the North Sea.	13	1
201509	1431	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	So if supply adjustments are required, which we think they will be, they are going to need to take place mostly in the United States.	13	1
201509	1432	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	In our view, this is going to be challenging and very painful economically, and it is going to be primarily in the area of the shale producers.	13	1
201509	1433	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	In response to all of this, producers, as you would expect, are cutting their capital outlays—in some cases, for the second or third time.	13	1
201509	1434	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	For North America as a whole, we expect energy industry cap ex to fall as much as 10 to 15 percent in 2016 versus 2015.	13	1
201509	1435	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Despite the initial surge of capital that came into the sector early this year, multiple Beige Book contacts reported that the credit situation is in fact worsening for many small- to mid-cap independent producers.	13	1
201509	1436	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	And potential new capital is now resetting its expectations much more realistically to lower prices for longer.	13	1
201509	1437	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	We believe this will likely lead to more defaults, debt restructurings, and merger activity.	13	1
201509	1438	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Based on all of these factors, it is our view that it may not be until sometime in 2017 that global supply and demand get into some reasonable degree of balance.	13	1
201509	1439	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	With that backdrop, let me talk about the Eleventh District.	13	1
201509	1440	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	There certainly will continue to be negative spillovers from all of this in the Eleventh District.	13	1
201509	1441	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	We see it in the manufacturing survey, and, in fact, our most recent survey shows that the new orders component dropped 13 points to negative 12½ after having reached positive territory in July for the first time this year.	13	1
201509	1442	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	The service sector is stronger and more resilient and still growing at close to its expansion average, but we are seeing signs that retail sales are beginning to weaken.	13	1
201509	1443	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	In addition to the effect of the energy sector, Beige Book contacts suggest some of this retail weakness is due to the strength of the dollar, which really affects Texas maybe more than other states because it hurts the purchasing power of Mexican shoppers who contribute significantly to retail sales in the state of Texas.	13	1
201509	1444	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Despite all of this, employment in the Eleventh District has been surprisingly resilient, probably because of the diversified nature of the economy.	13	1
201509	1445	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Even factoring in these negative energy developments, our regional economists still predict that Texas jobs will grow at an annualized pace of 1.3 percent over the final five months of this year, which is the same rate as the first seven months.	13	1
201509	1446	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Although reductions in energy-related jobs have been a negative factor, as of yet they have not affected the regional unemployment rate as much as we would have expected.	13	1
201509	1447	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	What is happening is that many of the people who moved to the area to work in the oil fields have now left and returned to their previous locations.	13	1
201509	1448	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Those who have remained have taken lower-paying jobs in other sectors, which, until recently, have struggled to attract new employees.	13	1
201509	1449	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	One of the pronounced features of our District is severe labor shortages in various areas—construction trades, manufacturing, food, nursing, truck driving, retail, and restaurants.	13	1
201509	1450	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Because of that, despite all of these negative factors from energy, we still see upward wage pressure.	13	1
201509	1451	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	And, related to that, we see a very strong real estate market.	13	1
201509	1452	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	If you look at the areas of the state which are less dependent on energy, the real estate sector remains robust.	13	1
201509	1453	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Our latest reading of Texas home values is up 8 percent year over year in the second quarter.	13	1
201509	1454	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	And we didn’t see much deceleration from quarter to quarter during the first two quarters of this year.	13	1
201509	1455	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	With that, downward price pressures actually accelerated notably in surveys in August.	13	1
201509	1456	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	According to our manufacturing surveys, and in the service sector, our selling price index slipped below zero, which is its first negative reading in nearly five years.	13	1
201509	1457	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	So, with all of this, there are a lot of crosscurrents in the state.	13	1
201509	1458	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	But all in all, even though the Eleventh District has remained resilient, we believe the negative effects of a potentially lower oil price for longer are continuing to unfold, and that probably means the risks in the District are to the downside.	13	1
201509	1459	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Turning to the national economy, we expect to see the unemployment rate reach its longer-term sustainable level by the end of this year—that is, 5 percent—and then fall below that level.	13	1
201509	1460	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	With unemployment low and falling, and with longer-run inflation expectations well anchored, we believe inflation should begin moving up toward our 2 percent objective as the effects of the fall in oil and the rise of the dollar eventually pass through inflation calculations.	13	1
201509	1461	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	By the end of 2017, we believe we are going to be very likely near our inflation target of 2 percent.	13	1
201509	1462	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	We believe conditions outside the United States do pose a real threat to the scenario I just described, though.	13	1
201509	1463	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Major economies—including China, Europe, Brazil, and Japan, for example—face serious demographic, fiscal, and structural challenges.	13	1
201509	1464	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	These challenges have the potential to create spillovers, which could negatively affect the United States, and we believe these challenges are likely to take years versus months to unfold and address.	13	1
201509	1465	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Lastly, regarding the recent volatility in US and other global financial markets, for us this is not, as of yet, a major factor in our assessment of overall conditions, and let me explain why.	13	1
201509	1466	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Although a decline in market value certainly could have negative wealth effects, we believe it has to be viewed in the context of overall valuation levels.	13	1
201509	1467	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	And, in that regard, we believe valuations heading into the summer were fulsome by historical standards—certainly in the United States, but you can make the same argument about non-US markets, maybe even to a greater degree.	13	1
201509	1468	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	When we look at expected earnings, price/earnings ratios, and other key valuation factors, we believe that, in that context, an equity market correction like the one we recently had could potentially be healthy and, in fact, indicative of appropriate reassessment of risk‒return by market participants.	13	1
201509	1469	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Thank you.	13	1

201509	1481	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Each had stronger expectations for the year back in January.	13	1
201509	1482	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	We did hear a few other notes of caution.	13	1
201509	1483	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	United Airlines reported that business travel was down for the entire industry.	13	1
201509	1484	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	And Manpower Employment Services said orders for temp workers have softened, reflecting clients’ uncertainty about the demand for their products.	13	1

201509	1486	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Similarly, wage gains were confined to these hard-to-fill occupations.	13	1
201509	1487	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	On the international front, most contacts expressed caution about the prospects for global growth.	13	1

201509	1489	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The gains, though, are coming from low levels.	13	1
201509	1490	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Not surprisingly, just about everyone was pessimistic about China, and there were some dire comments about Latin America, especially Brazil, which one large manufacturer described as “going off a cliff.”	13	1
201509	1491	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Turning to the national outlook, my own assessment has not changed a great deal.	13	1
201509	1492	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I expect growth will average about 2½ percent over the forecast period.	13	1
201509	1493	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	That is above the Tealbook, reflecting in part my somewhat higher path for potential output.	13	1
201509	1494	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I expect the unemployment rate will fall to 5 percent by the end of this year, which would match my assessment for the current level of the natural rate.	13	1
201509	1495	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I agree with the Tealbook that, on net, other labor market indicators point to some additional slack beyond what the unemployment rate shows.	13	1
201509	1496	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But I expect these gaps will diminish, too, as we move through this year and next.	13	1
201509	1497	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But inflation continues to be another story.	13	1
201509	1498	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I think we are still quite a way from reasonable confidence that inflation will rise to target over the medium term.	13	1
201509	1499	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Indeed, the news since July has been disappointing.	13	1
201509	1500	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	We have been expecting that the disinflationary influences of energy and import prices would dissipate soon.	13	1
201509	1501	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Instead, over the intermeeting period, oil prices and the dollar have broken in the “wrong” direction.	13	1
201509	1502	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The glimmer of higher wage growth we thought we saw in the ECI in the first quarter also has vanished.	13	1
201509	1503	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	President Rosengren was pretty accurate in forecasting this second-quarter change at our previous meeting.	13	1
201509	1504	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	And the year-over-year increase in core PCE inflation is still just 1.2 percent.	13	1
201509	1505	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Not long ago, some were putting more emphasis on three-month inflation, which had picked up.	13	1
201509	1506	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Now the three-month change in core PCE has moved back down.	13	1
201509	1507	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The Tealbook speculated that the elevated second-quarter core number was an aberration, in part due to residual seasonality, and that was a pretty good call.	13	1
201509	1508	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	My own forecast is very close to the Tealbook.	13	1
201509	1509	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I also see inflation only slowly marching up to 1.9 percent in 2018.	13	1
201509	1510	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But getting up to this 1.9 percent inflation assessment continues to be tough for me.	13	1
201509	1511	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	None of the inflation models we regularly run at the Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago get us to 2 percent within the forecast horizon.	13	1
201509	1512	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Nonetheless, like the Tealbook, and like most of us around this table, my judgmental forecast embeds the assumption that inflation expectations will exert a substantial upward pull on actual inflation.	13	1
201509	1513	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But this projection is fraught with uncertainties.	13	1
201509	1514	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The recent memo by Travis Berge, Brad Strum, and Kei-Mu Yi summarized the inflation models used around the Federal Reserve System.	13	1
201509	1515	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The collection of models reported suggests that one needs to put a good deal of weight on survey measures of long-term PCE inflation expectations, which are flat at 2 percent, in order to get a model projection up to target.	13	1
201509	1516	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But relying on long-term inflation expectations isn’t always enough.	13	1
201509	1517	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	As I have discussed here before, our Chicago DSGE model also uses the SPF 10-year CPI expectations to inform its latent inflation trend.	13	1
201509	1518	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The declines in those long-term CPI expectations over the past year and a half as well as other data keep the model’s core PCE inflation forecast down at only 1½ percent in 2018.	13	1
201509	1519	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	In a somewhat similar vein, the Board staff’s long-run inflation attractor is currently anchored at 1.8 percent rather than 2 percent.	13	1
201509	1520	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I still find that worrisome.	13	1
201509	1521	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Taken together, these results highlight that current survey inflation expectations could be less helpful than we think, and, to the degree that they are less helpful, any slippage in long-term inflation expectations could put our inflation forecast at even greater risk.	13	1
201509	1522	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	An important ingredient in my SEP forecast is that we avoid such slippage, and that we instead have long-term expectations that are firmly anchored at our inflation target.	13	1
201509	1523	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	It is crucial, then, that the public’s inflation expectations be well supported by monetary policy.	13	1
201509	1524	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	In my SEP forecast, long-term inflation expectations are anchored by a policy rate path that aggressively aims to achieve our symmetric inflation target and is not overly averse to inflation outcomes that run moderately above 2 percent.	13	1
201509	1525	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Given what we know today, in my SEP forecast such a policy is consistent with a mid-2016 liftoff in the funds rate and a subsequent shallow path that reaches 3 percent by the end of 2018.	13	1
201509	1526	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	My premise is that it will be the middle of next year before we and the public finally see core inflation moving up more consistently.	13	1
201509	1527	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	By then, I hope we will also have experienced a few months of relative quiet on the energy and dollar front.	13	1
201509	1528	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	This delayed liftoff also provides some extra buffer against important downside risks to the outlook.	13	1
201509	1529	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201509	1593	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My sense, too, is that the Committee’s unwillingness to communicate openly about its post-liftoff framework tends to foster this perception among outsiders that we are going to go back to the way business was conducted before 2008.	13	1
201509	1594	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am going to suggest over the next couple of days that this would be a mistake.	13	1
201509	1595	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, a good policy framework should automatically engender something that approximates a desirable monetary policy response to severe shocks like the one that hit the economy in 2008.	13	1
201509	1596	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Our pre-2008 policy framework failed in this dimension.	13	1
201509	1597	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It led the Committee to deliberately promulgate persistent shortfalls in prices and employment.	13	1
201509	1598	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What I’ll do today is point out what I see as being the key conceptual flaw in the pre-2008 framework, and tomorrow I will suggest what I see as a better framework and describe what that better framework would imply for current decisions.	13	1
201509	1599	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To understand my criticism of the pre-2008 framework, it’s useful to go back to the November 2009 meeting, which was the very beginning of the recovery.	13	1
201509	1600	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At that meeting, the latest unemployment reading was 9.8 percent and the staff’s nowcast for core inflation was 1.4 percent.	13	1
201509	1601	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The median participant’s assessment was that, under appropriate monetary policy, the unemployment rate would still be 7 percent in three years.	13	1
201509	1602	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At the same time, the median participant’s assessment was that, under appropriate monetary policy, PCE inflation would only rise back to 1½ percent three years later.	13	1
201509	1603	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So, three years later, we had unemployment at 7 percent and inflation at 1½ percent.	13	1
201509	1604	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	When I was reading these numbers, I found them quite surprising.	13	1
201509	1605	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	You can draw one of two conclusions from them.	13	1
201509	1606	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	On the one hand, you can say that the Committee was willing, in November 2009, to forgo the timely creation of hundreds of thousands, possibly millions, of jobs in the absence of any inflationary threat that was perceived by the Committee.	13	1
201509	1607	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	On the other hand, you can focus only on the price-stability mandate and say that monetary policy can’t do much about unemployment.	13	1
201509	1608	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That is a view that has been expressed around this table before.	13	1
201509	1609	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Or, you can focus only on the price stability mandate and say that the Committee was willing to make policy choices and put the credibility of its then-informal 2 percent target in jeopardy.	13	1
201509	1610	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	However you put it, it is hard to understand these projections—7 percent unemployment and 1½ percent inflation three years later—as representing the outcome of appropriate monetary policy.	13	1
201509	1611	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Why did the Committee view such a persistent and extreme shortfall with respect to its objectives as being appropriate?	13	1
201509	1612	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A quick side note:  Labor market recovery actually turned out to be much worse than that.	13	1
201509	1613	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Unemployment was 7.8 percent three years later, and labor force participation declined much more than the Committee anticipated—or anyone else anticipated, for that matter.	13	1
201509	1614	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Inflation ended up being around what the Committee viewed as being desirable—thanks, I think, in no little part, to choices made by the Committee.	13	1
201509	1615	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But why did the Committee, in November 2009, view such a persistent extreme shortfall with respect to its objectives as being appropriate?	13	1
201509	1616	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The answer, I believe, lies in the pre-2008 policy framework, which centered on variants of the Taylor (1993) rule.	13	1
201509	1617	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And this framework continues to live on in the collection of interest rate rules that we see in Tealbook B.	13	1
201509	1618	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, all of these rules have a key conceptual shortcoming.	13	1
201509	1619	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Committee has a dual mandate, which is to promote price stability and maximum employment.	13	1
201509	1620	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Taylor rules are based on the presumption that the Committee has other objectives in terms of the time path of interest rates that are independent of the objectives for employment and prices.	13	1
201509	1621	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The original Taylor (1993) rule implicitly presumes that the Committee does not like interest rate gaps.	13	1
201509	1622	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The FOMC desires to keep the federal funds rate close to its long-run level.	13	1
201509	1623	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The rule then trades off the Committee’s unmandated aversion to interest rate gaps against its mandated aversion to unemployment and inflation gaps.	13	1
201509	1624	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Otherwise, if you saw unemployment and inflation gaps going in the same direction—unemployment too high, inflation too low—you should just lower rates some more.	13	1
201509	1625	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But the Taylor rule says, wait a second, you shouldn’t be doing that, because actually you don’t want to move interest rates around too much.	13	1
201509	1626	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The way that the Taylor rule resolves this tradeoff—interest rate volatility and gap volatility—especially when the Phillips curve is as flat as it’s proven to be, can result in very odd outcomes.	13	1
201509	1627	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So, in November 2009, the staff’s outlook was based on the Taylor (1993) rule.	13	1
201509	1628	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That outlook had unemployment above the natural rate for four years and inflation at or below 1.6 percent for five years.	13	1
201509	1629	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We didn’t get to see the staff outlook beyond a five-year horizon, so I don’t have any sense of when it ever got back to 2 percent.	13	1
201509	1630	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My reading of the transcript, in terms of participants’ contributions, is that aversion to accommodation, as opposed to inflation or unemployment, was really at the heart of that discussion.	13	1
201509	1631	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The big debate at that meeting was, should we plan to raise rates when the unemployment rate is in the 9s or in the 8s?	13	1
201509	1632	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Summary of Economic Projections shows that the key motivating factor for this debate was not really inflation.	13	1
201509	1633	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Rather, it was the Committee’s willingness to give up on its dual-mandate goals in order to get back to normalizing policy more rapidly.	13	1
201509	1634	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Madam Chair, the Federal Reserve did such a heroic job of successfully healing extraordinary financial market turmoil in the latter part of the past decade.	13	1
201509	1635	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But our monetary policy response was not as successful.	13	1
201509	1636	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I attribute this to the Committee’s policy framework, which deliberately directed the economy toward relatively persistent large employment and inflation shortfalls.	13	1
201509	1637	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we need to have a policy framework that works considerably better in the face of adverse shocks than we had available in November 2009.	13	1
201509	1638	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I have argued today that shortcomings of our pre-2008 framework can be traced to its reliance on variants of the Taylor rule.	13	1
201509	1639	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These rules implicitly impose a large penalty on historically unusual settings of the federal funds rate and other forms of accommodation.	13	1
201509	1640	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need to have a policy framework that is much less averse to an unusual use of our tools as opposed to achieving our objectives.	13	1
201509	1641	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Tomorrow I will talk about such a framework and some of its implications for our current decisionmaking.	13	1
201509	1642	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1643	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201509	1644	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	13	1
201509	1645	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1646	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Just going back to President Kocherlakota’s comments, I don’t remember November 2009 quite that way.	13	1
201509	1647	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Just for the record, we didn’t have tools at the time that could generate a more rapid return, and we were gradually inventing them.	13	1
201509	1648	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We had already cut the funds rate target to zero.	13	1
201509	1649	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We had already engaged in some asset purchases.	13	1
201509	1650	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The way I remember it, I think it’s fair to say, it took a while before we decided we could and should really scale up our asset purchases—	13	1
201509	1651	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Yes.	13	1
201509	1652	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	We learned by doing.	13	1
201509	1653	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	—yes—and use more unconventional forms of forward guidance that would push expectations way out.	13	1
201509	1654	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Our toolkit today has a much better, deeper set of tools to help us achieve our objectives than the one we had in November 2009 did.	13	1

201509	1657	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	But anyway—	13	1
201509	1658	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is a great conversation.	13	1

201509	1662	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A lot of the surveys, for example, done by the Open Market Desk had a number of primary dealers seeing interest rates going up when the unemployment rate was still in the 9s.	13	1
201509	1663	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There were tools that were under our control and at our disposal.	13	1

201509	1665	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	And beyond.	13	1
201509	1666	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	[Laughter]	13	1
201509	1667	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Over many drinks.	13	1
201509	1668	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Okay.	13	1
201509	1669	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Switching gears, as far as I’m concerned, the economy has been on essentially the same trajectory now that it has been on for some time, growth slightly above trend and sufficient to lead to a gradual tightening in the labor market.	13	1
201509	1670	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	To me, the key question is whether this is going to continue.	13	1
201509	1671	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	When I look at the key sectors of the economy, I agree with others.	13	1
201509	1672	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Consumer spending seems to have relatively firm underpinnings because it has solid job gains and low inflation, and the inflation shocks actually are boosting real income.	13	1
201509	1673	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The housing sector also seems to be a positive, with activity encouraged by strengthening sales and rising prices.	13	1
201509	1674	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Sturdy job gains and low mortgage rates have provided, I think, significant support for the sector, and I certainly expect the housing sector to continue to recover over the year ahead.	13	1
201509	1675	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Nevertheless, I do think there are risks in terms of growth, and I think they’ve very much swung to the downside.	13	1
201509	1676	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Despite what I think is a relatively sturdy second-quarter GDP report, I believe the economy has somewhat less forward momentum than maybe some others around the table think, and, most significantly, I think the risks around that baseline outlook are tilted to the downside.	13	1
201509	1677	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Turning to the economic growth outlook, I think there are a number of reasons for concern.	13	1
201509	1678	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Most importantly, we do have a quite dicey international situation, with growth slowing in China and commodity prices weakening broadly, and I think this is putting considerable strain on a wide array of emerging market economies.	13	1
201509	1679	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, last week we had the downgrade of Brazil’s sovereign debt rating to junk bond status by S&P.	13	1
201509	1680	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So we’ll see how that actually plays out.	13	1
201509	1681	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think generally what’s happening is that we’re undergoing a pretty significant regime shift from a few years ago when strong Chinese demand was keeping commodity prices well above the marginal cost of new production.	13	1
201509	1682	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The result was a very favorable terms-of-trade shift for many EMEs that are commodity producers and a very strong impetus to investment in those countries.	13	1
201509	1683	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, all of that has been reversing, and I think the risks are that the consequences for global growth could turn out to be stronger and longer lasting than we’d expected.	13	1
201509	1684	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The terms-of-trade reversal we’ve already seen is leading to a sharp slowdown in EME growth, currency weakness, a deterioration in many countries’ fiscal positions, and significant political stress.	13	1
201509	1685	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think there is a nonnegligible risk of an unfavorable dynamic that could persist for some time.	13	1
201509	1686	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So let me just sketch this out.	13	1
201509	1687	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m not saying this is going to happen, I just think there’s some probability mass on this outcome.	13	1
201509	1688	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Weakness in commodity prices leads to further stress on many EMEs.	13	1
201509	1689	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That leads to corporate difficulties, which we haven’t seen much of yet, further capital flight, and further currency weakness.	13	1
201509	1690	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	For us, it means that dollar strength persists, and this erodes our own growth momentum and puts further downward pressure on inflation.	13	1
201509	1691	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, the strong dollar increases the stress on EME corporates that have significant dollar-denominated debt exposure.	13	1
201509	1692	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The stronger dollar also squeezes US profit margins, leading to weaker corporate earnings and a softer US equity market.	13	1
201509	1693	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	US financial conditions keep tightening.	13	1
201509	1694	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t know how much weight to put on this scenario, but what I think is interesting about this scenario is that it has several important reinforcing feedback loops.	13	1
201509	1695	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	We saw in the financial crisis that that’s how you can get pretty bad outcomes.	13	1
201509	1696	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	It strikes me that the risks here are not zero.	13	1
201509	1697	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	When we went around the table, a lot of people were just saying, “There’s stuff going on in the markets.”	13	1
201509	1698	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the markets are reflecting fundamental developments that are occurring in the global economy, and as a consequence of that, I take those financial market developments more seriously.	13	1
201509	1699	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Financial conditions have already tightened significantly as the dollar has appreciated on a broad trade-weighted basis, and the US equity market has weakened.	13	1
201509	1700	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I, like others, don’t put much weight on the equity market decline yet because it hasn’t been in place for very long, but the dollar strength has been persistent and does threaten to undermine US net exports.	13	1
201509	1701	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m particularly struck by the weakness of the Canadian dollar and the Mexican peso versus the US dollar because we generally think that those countries have pretty good economic policy and institutional structures.	13	1
201509	1702	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Yet currently the Canadian dollar trades at 1.32 per US dollar; a year ago it was at 1.10.	13	1
201509	1703	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The same for the Mexican peso, which has depreciated about 30 percent over the past year and nearly 10 percent over the past three months.	13	1
201509	1704	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	These are two major US trading partners whose currency has moved a lot, and I don’t think we’ve really seen the consequences of that in terms of our trade.	13	1
201509	1705	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Moreover, apart from international developments, I think there are other reasons to be concerned about the growth outlook.	13	1
201509	1706	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So let’s just set aside the international stuff for a minute.	13	1
201509	1707	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	First, job gains have been strong relative to the underlying growth trajectory.	13	1
201509	1708	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	People have said, “Well, that’s just going to continue.”	13	1
201509	1709	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s not obvious to me that that would continue because one thing that is happening is, profit growth is really slowing down.	13	1
201509	1710	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	And we’ve heard that a number of corporations are now really looking at how they are going to raise earnings, and maybe they’re going to have to start being tougher and begin to think about downsizing.	13	1
201509	1711	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, I think we’ve had a pretty significant climb in inventory investment, and that provided a significant contribution to growth in the first half of the year.	13	1
201509	1712	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In the second quarter, the real nonfarm inventory build was almost $120 billion at an annual rate.	13	1
201509	1713	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s probably more than double what’s sustainable over the longer term.	13	1
201509	1714	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Third, earlier this year, we were talking about how the household savings rate seemed high relative to what was implied by the historical relationship between household net worth and disposable income.	13	1
201509	1715	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That was making us feel more optimistic about consumption, that consumption could grow faster than income for a time because the household savings rate was high.	13	1
201509	1716	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	But after revisions, it doesn’t look high anymore.	13	1
201509	1717	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	We’re back at 4.8 percent of disposable income.	13	1
201509	1718	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s the same level we saw in 2013 and 2014, so I don’t think we have so much support from that.	13	1
201509	1719	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to inflation, with the exception of the softness in commodity prices, I also don’t think the situation has changed much, and I don’t think it is particularly worrisome as long as the economy continues to grow at an above-trend pace.	13	1
201509	1720	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	If you could guarantee that the economy was going to grow at an above-trend pace, I wouldn’t be that worried about the inflation outlook, but because I’m worried about the strength of US growth, that does make me worry about the mechanism that’s going to push inflation back up toward our objective.	13	1
201509	1721	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The fact is that, despite falling energy prices and weaker import prices, the trend for core inflation has flattened out.	13	1
201509	1722	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	This suggests to me that if growth does remain above trend, then the low inflation problem will take care of itself.	13	1
201509	1723	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	That said, the fact that nominal wage growth has not picked up yet implies that we still, in my mind, have excess slack in the labor market.	13	1
201509	1724	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Combined with the sluggish growth trend and the downside risk to growth threatened by international developments, this suggests to me that the costs of waiting, in terms of beginning monetary policy normalization, are pretty low right now.	13	1
201509	1725	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	My preference would be to wait a bit longer so we can better assess the consequences of developments in China and among the EMEs in terms of the implications regarding US growth and inflation.	13	1
201509	1726	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	As I see it, the risks around liftoff right now are asymmetric.	13	1
201509	1727	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	If we go now and the international market developments prove to be of sufficient intensity to deflect the US economy away from our objectives, the cost could be quite high to us.	13	1
201509	1728	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Conversely, if we wait a little bit longer and the effect turns out to be insignificant, then we can go before year-end, and I don’t really think we give up much in terms of our ability to achieve our objectives.	13	1
201509	1729	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Speaking for myself, I won’t feel particularly bad if we waited and then it turns out everything is fine.	13	1
201509	1730	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I think I’ll feel pretty good about that.	13	1
201509	1731	2015-09-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201509	1733	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	13	1
201509	1734	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1735	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	My views about the likely trajectories of economic activity and inflation are not very different from the views I held in July.	13	1
201509	1736	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I believed then that we were closing in on full employment, and I believe that is even more true today.	13	1
201509	1737	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	And I said then that I was reasonably confident that inflation would move back toward 2 percent in the not-too-distant future, and that is still my view.	13	1
201509	1738	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	However, like most of you, I’ve become more concerned about the situation abroad over the past several weeks, and this leads me to attach more downside risk to my projection than I would have done at our previous meeting.	13	1
201509	1739	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The effect of foreign developments has been reasonably small so far, though, of course, these developments may well take longer to affect us than the short period since China’s exchange rate adjustment, and we shall simply have to keep monitoring these developments.	13	1
201509	1740	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	There has been a lot of discussion about inflation over the intermeeting period and during this meeting so far.	13	1
201509	1741	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is no surprise, considering that this is the part of our mandate on which we are most obviously missing our target, and so I’d like to focus the remainder of my remarks today on inflation.	13	1
201509	1742	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Many discussions of inflation start with the 12-month core PCE inflation rate, which is currently 1.2 percent and projected to be 1.3 percent by the end of the year, although total PCE inflation is projected to be only 0.3 percent at that time.	13	1
201509	1743	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The main reason for the 1 percentage point difference between the core and the total rates of PCE inflation arises from the recent declines in oil prices, which are expected to be temporary.	13	1
201509	1744	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	However, changes in oil prices have an effect on PCE prices that goes beyond the prices that are excluded by using the core PCE inflation rate.	13	1
201509	1745	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Oil prices affect the cost of production of many goods.	13	1
201509	1746	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Moreover, the appreciation of the dollar has direct effects on the prices of many goods.	13	1
201509	1747	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The additional effect of recent changes in oil and import prices on the inflation rate— over and above what’s picked up in food and energy prices—is estimated by staff at approximately 0.4 percentage point this year.	13	1
201509	1748	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Accordingly, we can conclude that the declines in oil and import prices together have reduced the overall inflation rate by approximately 1.4 percentage points.	13	1
201509	1749	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	More-rigorous methods of stripping out the transitory factors, such as using the Dallas Fed trimmed mean PCE or a weighted median PCE price index and other measures, yield a reasonably similar conclusion on balance.	13	1
201509	1750	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	But regardless of the exact figure we use, I think that a good portion of the factors holding down underlying inflation are transitory, the result of changes in oil and other commodity prices and of the exchange rate.	13	1
201509	1751	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	If the exchange rate stops appreciating, and that is highly likely, its downward pressure on core inflation will gradually stop.	13	1
201509	1752	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Similarly, if the price of oil eventually stops decreasing, its drag on core inflation will also abate.	13	1
201509	1753	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Although it’s difficult to predict when the exchange rate and the price of oil will stop rising and falling, respectively, it is almost certain that current trends in these two variables will stop in the medium term.	13	1
201509	1754	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	As a result, I am reasonably confident that inflation will move back toward 2 percent in the medium term.	13	1
201509	1755	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I leave the rest for tomorrow, Madam Chair.	13	1
201509	1756	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you.	13	1

201509	1767	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	To the contrary, they’re really quite good at what they do, but it’s a difficult situation, and whenever you’re in a difficult situation, there are no great policy options.	13	1
201509	1768	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	My impression is that the thing that worries Chinese officials most in the near term is the amount of margining that lies behind a lot of those holdings in equity markets, and the margining is connected very directly to the amount of credit extended through the shadow banking system.	13	1
201509	1769	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think what is less fully realized is how closely that connects to the regular regulated banking system as well in China.	13	1

201509	1772	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	So, I think, as Bill was suggesting, it’s what lies behind both the market movements and the policy responses and some of the policy uncertainty about the market movements that suggests potential for longer-term problems.	13	1

201509	1775	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	I want to spend the rest of my time on labor markets, and having made a joke about what Narayana is doing, I’m going to proceed to do something not dissimilar, which is to try to give a bit of perspective on how we’ve been assessing labor markets, not monetary policy as a whole.	13	1
201509	1776	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	There is a lot of talk within this room, by many of you outside this room, and by many other people about how we are close to or at fill-in-the-blank:  the natural rate, full employment, maximum employment, whatever it may be.	13	1
201509	1777	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	And what I want to know is, how do people know this?	13	1
201509	1778	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	I mean, it is tautological to say that we’re closer to full employment, maximum employment, the natural rate, than we were at the July meeting and the June meeting and the meetings before that because, during this period, unemployment has been going down and job creation has been such that we’re creating more jobs than the number of entrants into the labor market.	13	1
201509	1779	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Almost tautologically, we are closer.	13	1
201509	1780	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But how much closer are we, and how do we know how much slack remains?	13	1
201509	1781	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Conventionally, the way in which we collectively made judgments about labor market tightness or getting to the natural rate or getting to the non-accelerating inflation rate of unemployment was by looking at prices or, oftentimes, actually, more directly at wages, which were thought to be a leading indicator of prices.	13	1
201509	1782	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Remember that the “I” in NAIRU stands for inflation, and that was where we and other analysts were trying to make that connection.	13	1
201509	1783	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Now, I didn’t count, but six or seven of you referred to wage pressures being reported from your Districts.	13	1
201509	1784	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	I have to say, a number of presidents have been reporting wage pressures from their Districts for some years now, and I take it to be the case that the number of you now talking about it suggests that we may be closer to the point at which wage pressures start translating into the data.	13	1
201509	1785	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But as of this moment, they really haven’t translated into the data as a whole.	13	1
201509	1786	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	That, of course, is a reminder of what people have also commented on, which is that the Phillips curve broke down as a predictor of what would happen to inflation based on unemployment well before the crisis and the recession, during a period in which labor markets were changing significantly in what quite likely seems to have been a secular, rather than a purely cyclical, fashion.	13	1
201509	1787	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Now, people, including the people around this table and their staffs, have subsequently made efforts to assess labor market tightness based on some set of past relationships, but to date I don’t think these relationships really panned out as particularly robust.	13	1
201509	1788	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	It’s not the fault of anybody.	13	1
201509	1789	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think anybody knows what those relationships are now.	13	1
201509	1790	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	A few years ago around this table, I remember people were talking about how the persistence of the rightward shift in the Beveridge curve showed that there was structural unemployment and, therefore, the natural rate must be higher, and we were all of a sudden going to begin seeing wage inflation.	13	1
201509	1791	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	That didn’t happen, right?	13	1
201509	1792	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Remember there was a suggestion a couple of years ago that since short-term unemployment rates were now back to pre-recession levels, we were functionally getting close to the natural rate of unemployment.	13	1
201509	1793	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	It was a good try, but that one didn’t work out either.	13	1
201509	1794	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	President Williams has just suggested another approach—to use demographics and try to project where the “natural rate” would lie.	13	1
201509	1795	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But I think if you disconnect the concept of the natural rate of unemployment from at least wage inflation, if not price inflation, then the whole concept actually gets more than a little bit squishy, because what is it that we’re talking about now?	13	1
201509	1796	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Are we talking about “satisficing” unemployment?	13	1
201509	1797	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Do we think it’s good enough, it’s low enough?	13	1
201509	1798	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think we’re not actually any longer in the realm of doing analysis, but instead acting on some intuition.	13	1
201509	1799	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Just because U-3 is toward the low end of where it has been over the course of the past couple of decades doesn’t tell us much.	13	1

201509	1802	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	For me, this dilemma—and I mean to project it as a dilemma rather than people being wrong, because we’re all wrong, in a sense, because nobody actually has a convincing set of explanations.	13	1
201509	1803	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But for me, it was crystallized in the staff briefing to the Board at yesterday’s meeting when I noticed that the projected path of wages over the next couple of years was rising, and the explanation given in the briefing was not principally because of labor market tightness, but because productivity gains would be passed through and inflation would pull up wages.	13	1
201509	1804	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Of course, I asked about the productivity gains issue because, I think my understanding is that productivity gains matter for how much wages can go up over the medium-to-long term, but in the short term, wages really should be about the supply and demand of labor rather than near- term productivity increases.	13	1
201509	1805	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But even so, productivity gains clearly haven’t been passed through in anything like one-to-one or even 50 percent fashion in recent years.	13	1
201509	1806	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	They might be at some point, but it’s a little hard to predict.	13	1

201509	1809	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	It came from inflation expectations, and we’re back, as David Wilcox noted a little earlier this afternoon, into a reliance on a mechanism that we don’t completely understand, and what we really don’t understand is how those expectations change.	13	1
201509	1810	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	They seem to have worked, and I think the reason the staff has hit upon the approach they’ve taken is, they’ve found some things that had been working reasonably well over the past five or six years.	13	1
201509	1811	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Assuming anchored expectations and assuming that the now-low productivity gains will get passed through seems to be working, but not because there’s a theory regarding why this is all working this way.	13	1
201509	1812	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Instead, it just kind of seems to be working.	13	1

201509	1815	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But in the absence of that theoretical understanding that comports with empirically observed facts, we’re left not knowing whether we’re just in an extended period of reversion to a certain set of correlations and causal relationships that existed for a long enough time to produce a bunch of economic laws and curves that then find their way into people’s textbooks, or whether the changes that have been noticed in labor markets over the past 15 to 20 years have now cumulatively created a new set of correlations and causal relationships that are nontransitory and that we don’t fully understand.	13	1

201509	1895	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	On the other hand, the foreign economic outlook, I think, has again contributed materially to financial tightening and poses downside risks to the outlook.	13	1
201509	1896	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	We see no indication of an acceleration in either wages or prices, and inflation remains stubbornly below our target.	13	1
201509	1897	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Let me just spend a moment on each of these.	13	1
201509	1898	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	As you all have noted, the labor market has continued to improve nicely.	13	1
201509	1899	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The three-month moving average of payroll employment growth was 220,000 in August, similar to average gains so far this year, and August payrolls are likely to be revised up.	13	1
201509	1900	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, there continues to be improvement, on balance, along the three main margins of labor market slack.	13	1
201509	1901	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Despite this, the ongoing diminution of slack has yet to result in any noticeable acceleration in our three broad measures of wages.	13	1
201509	1902	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Average hourly earnings through August as well as compensation per hour and the employment cost index through the second quarter all suggest that nominal wage growth is only in the 2 to 2¼ percent range, which is little different than the pace we have seen over the past several years.	13	1
201509	1903	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The absence of such acceleration suggests that resources still are not fully utilized, and I think other data send a similar signal.	13	1
201509	1904	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Participation for prime-age adults remains well below pre-recession levels and below what pre-crisis trends in participation for this group would suggest.	13	1
201509	1905	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The share of employees working part time for economic reasons remains well above longer-run norms, even allowing for some move-up in the equilibrium level in recent years.	13	1
201509	1906	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	As others have pointed out, although it is difficult to know with any precision what the natural rate is, the absence in recent quarters of any upward movement in nominal wage growth and price inflation has to be seen as some indication that the natural rate is below the current level.	13	1
201509	1907	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And I think it’s interesting to note that since our submissions in June, it appears that nine Committee members—and I’m just staring at the dots—have moved their point estimates for the natural rate below 5 percent.	13	1
201509	1908	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	More broadly, domestic activity has been proceeding at a reassuring pace on most dimensions, suggesting demand is solid.	13	1
201509	1909	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Although inventory investment in the second quarter looks elevated, suggesting a negative contribution in the second half of the year, other components of business investment look better than they did in July.	13	1
201509	1910	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, nonresidential building investment rose strongly in the second quarter, offsetting the weakness that we had seen in drilling investment, and indicators of equipment investment have also turned up of late.	13	1
201509	1911	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Strong auto sales and growth in other components of retail sales suggest consumer spending is rising at a welcome pace moving into the second half.	13	1
201509	1912	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Continued job growth and lower gas prices should continue to support this.	13	1
201509	1913	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And the latest data on building permits and starts continue to paint a picture of gradual recovery in housing.	13	1
201509	1914	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Overall, despite an anemic contribution from government spending, domestic demand is advancing.	13	1
201509	1915	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Domestic final sales rose 2½ percent in the first half of 2015, and the Tealbook expects similar growth in the second half.	13	1
201509	1916	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	By contrast, manufacturing exports are on the soft side, and that brings me to the crosscurrents.	13	1
201509	1917	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Looking back over the past year, it is very clear that foreign economic conditions are weighing on real activity and inflation as well as on financial conditions in the United States.	13	1
201509	1918	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	At the end of last year, persistently weak aggregate demand in the euro zone and in Japan, as well as the policy response, were kind of the main story.	13	1
201509	1919	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	More recently, weakness in foreign demand has really focused on emerging market economies.	13	1
201509	1920	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Growing recognition of this weakness has pushed the dollar up further, so after the 12 percent we saw earlier, we now have an additional movement, and the dollar now lies 15 percent above its level last summer.	13	1
201509	1921	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	China, in particular, has been the focus of an intermeeting reassessment of global growth prospects.	13	1
201509	1922	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I think China’s contribution really has to be seen in the broader context of spillovers both in real activity and the financial sector, not directly through trade channels to the United States but as they reverberate around the global economy.	13	1
201509	1923	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, China has been at the center, really, of a commodity supercycle that has now endured for over a decade and has been a very important source of demand for many commodity exporters and is also very closely connected to many of the other neighboring economies in the region.	13	1
201509	1924	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Most immediately, the buildup of past property and more recent stock market bubbles, together with a rapid run-up in business debt levels and growing perceptions that Chinese policymakers are not managing policy or communications as deftly as previously anticipated, have raised concerns, I think, about broader global growth prospects and potential downside risks.	13	1
201509	1925	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And those risks are compounded and perhaps amplified by well-known weakness in the quality of macroeconomic data that, I think, risks perpetuating the fog around the growth trajectory.	13	1
201509	1926	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Looking forward, in terms of the US economy, I, like several other members of the Committee, really don’t see the intermeeting developments as narrow equity market corrections centered on the United States.	13	1
201509	1927	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I really see it as a broader reassessment of global growth prospects and questions about China’s trajectory.	13	1
201509	1928	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I think there is a nontrivial probability that we will see, sometime in the next few quarters, an additional adjustment of China’s exchange rate regime.	13	1
201509	1929	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I can’t tell you when or by how much, but it does seem like they are in the midst of an adjustment process, and that in turn is likely to reverberate, particularly because many other foreign economies facing weak internal demand—including in East Asia, the euro zone, and Japan—will have to adjust their policies accordingly.	13	1
201509	1930	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The direct and indirect effects of that further adjustment will remain a material risk to our own outlook.	13	1
201509	1931	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, my sense is that the effects of dollar appreciation, even the dollar appreciation we have seen so far, are likely to be quite persistent, and those effects, if the dollar appreciates further, are likely to lead to additional restraint both on real activity and on US inflation.	13	1
201509	1932	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	That comes against a backdrop in which US core PCE inflation remains quite subdued.	13	1
201509	1933	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The underlying trend, as many have noted, remains between maybe 1¼ to 1½ percent, similar to the pace that we have seen in the past couple of years and noticeably below our target.	13	1
201509	1934	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	If you look at the 12-month change in core PCE prices, or even if you look at the change in the Dallas Fed trimmed mean, we are still substantially below our target and have not made any progress.	13	1
201509	1935	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And although survey expectations provide some reassurance, the risks seem tilted to the downside, as inflation compensation has moved back to the historically low levels reached at the beginning of the year.	13	1
201509	1936	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	For all those reasons, I do see considerable value to waiting, and that value outweighs the cost.	13	1
201509	1937	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	But because we will have an opportunity to return to this tomorrow, I’d be particularly interested to hear from those who put the start of policy normalization in the third quarter of this year about the potential risks of waiting, because I think that would be helpful in informing my own policy outlook.	13	1

201509	1940	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I thought I would wrap things up, if you wouldn’t mind, by giving a summary of my own assessment of the incoming data and their implications for the outlook.	13	1
201509	1941	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Starting with the labor market, as almost all of you noted, we’ve seen continued solid gains in monthly payrolls.	13	1
201509	1942	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	And at 5.1 percent, the unemployment rate stands just a touch above the median of our estimates of its longer-run normal level.	13	1
201509	1943	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Broader measures of labor utilization like U-6 also have moved down as the number of discouraged workers continued to decline, and involuntary part-time employment edged down further.	13	1
201509	1944	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Consistent with the views I heard expressed around the table, I think these developments confirm that labor market conditions have improved considerably since earlier in the year.	13	1
201509	1945	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	For me, they’re also consistent with the conditions that, at the July meeting, I said in my own view could warrant raising the funds rate in September.	13	1
201509	1946	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	But back in July, I also indicated that stronger readings on wages would strengthen the case for liftoff, and instead, exactly the opposite has occurred.	13	1
201509	1947	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	And so, for me, wage developments weaken the case.	13	1
201509	1948	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	At the time, the available data seemed to suggest that wages were finally beginning to respond to diminishing slack.	13	1
201509	1949	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Since then, new readings on the ECI, hourly earnings, and compensation per hour all indicate that we’re still stuck at wage increases in the vicinity of 2 percent, a very subdued pace if the economy really is near full employment.	13	1
201509	1950	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I don’t want to make too much of the news.	13	1
201509	1951	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The relationship between nominal wage growth and slack is far from tight, and other factors you’ve mentioned around the table, such as weak productivity growth and global competition, may explain why wage gains remain anemic.	13	1
201509	1952	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Still, firms continue to attract and retain workers without raising wages, and even though we’ve seen an impressive increase in job openings, the quits rate has flattened out, and that is despite all the reports we hear about how difficult firms find it to fill some jobs.	13	1
201509	1953	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the margin, the disappointing wage data have reinforced my sense that we are still a ways from full employment, even if the economy is very close to the longer-run normal rate of unemployment.	13	1
201509	1954	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The current rate of involuntary part-time employment remains more than 1 percentage point above its pre-recession level, and the labor force participation rate remains below the staff’s estimate of its trend.	13	1
201509	1955	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Moreover, with the public dissatisfaction with the state of the labor market so widespread, I suspect that the current level of the trend participation rate is actually higher than the staff’s estimate, although I’m fairly confident in the trend’s downward slope, which I think can be estimated more reliably.	13	1
201509	1956	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Eliminating slack along these additional dimensions may well necessitate a temporary decline in the unemployment rate below its longer-run normal level.	13	1
201509	1957	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	For example, pulling discouraged workers back into the labor force may require a period of especially plentiful employment opportunities and strong hiring.	13	1
201509	1958	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Similarly, firms may be unwilling to restructure their operations to use more full-time workers until they encounter greater difficulty filling part- time positions.	13	1
201509	1959	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Beyond these dynamics, which effectively imply that the natural rate of unemployment is likely to run below its longer-run value for a time, a temporary undershooting of the longer-run level of unemployment could have other advantages, including speeding the return of inflation to 2 percent and even possibly reversing some of the adverse supply-side effects of recent years.	13	1
201509	1960	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Turning to growth, like most of you, I anticipate that labor market conditions will improve somewhat further over the rest of this year and into 2016, helped by continued moderate growth in real GDP.	13	1
201509	1961	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	My forecast is not too different from the one I had back in June.	13	1
201509	1962	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The data on spending and production received since then, in fact, have been somewhat stronger than I expected and—I think this coincides with what I heard around the table—stronger than what many of you expected.	13	1
201509	1963	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Most prominently, real GDP growth in the first half of the year has been revised up by more than 1 percentage point to 2¼ percent.	13	1
201509	1964	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Readings on consumer spending and residential construction into this summer have been solid, while the remarkable contraction in drilling activity appears to have bottomed out.	13	1
201509	1965	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Nonetheless, I would not describe overall growth as robust.	13	1
201509	1966	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	First, the strong growth in real GDP in the second quarter was most likely a payback for transitory weakness in the first.	13	1
201509	1967	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	And, second, overall growth is being held back by an appreciable and continuing drag generated by the behavior of net exports.	13	1
201509	1968	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	After factoring in the recent monthly trade data and the expected restraint from dollar appreciation and weak foreign growth, the staff estimates that real GDP is likely to expand at an annual rate of only 2 percent in the second half of the year and in 2016.	13	1
201509	1969	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	One implication of the incoming data and the near-term outlook is that the economy’s equilibrium real interest rate remains low and shows no obvious signs of rising this year.	13	1
201509	1970	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	That’s an inference that follows directly from the combination of continued moderate growth and a real funds rate that remains well below zero.	13	1
201509	1971	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	This stasis would seem to conflict with the story told by our medium-term forecasts, which imply a significant increase in the equilibrium real rate over the next few years as various headwinds restraining economic activity continue to fade.	13	1
201509	1972	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The explanation, of course, is that one headwind—namely, exchange rate appreciation and weak foreign growth—has strengthened over the past year.	13	1
201509	1973	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	This restraint has increased further since our previous meeting with the recent appreciation of the dollar, especially as it has been accompanied by an appreciable fall in stock prices and a modest rise in risk spreads on corporate bonds.	13	1
201509	1974	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	FRB/US model simulations suggest that these intermeeting financial and international developments, if they persist, would have demand effects similar to those generated by a 50 basis point hike in the federal funds rate.	13	1
201509	1975	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Whatever their implications for the modal outlook, recent movements in the dollar and other financial factors, coupled with increased concerns about the prospects for growth in China and the emerging market economies, certainly suggest that the downside risks to the US economy have increased to some degree, and several of you have noted the same thing.	13	1
201509	1976	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Turning to inflation, information received since our previous meeting, specifically lower oil prices and a higher dollar, suggests that the transitory factors currently holding down inflation are likely to fade a bit more slowly than I previously judged.	13	1
201509	1977	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	For example, the Tealbook now shows overall PCE inflation on a four-quarter basis running at only 1 percent through the first three quarters of next year.	13	1

201509	1979	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Nonetheless, I still expect that inflation will gradually return to 2 percent, provided—and this is key—that the labor market completes the return to full employment and long-run inflation expectations remain well anchored at 2 percent.	13	1
201509	1980	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	As I mentioned a moment ago, I anticipate that the labor market will continue to improve in coming quarters and, barring some adverse shock to the economy, I expect that the economy is likely to stay in the general vicinity of full employment over the medium term, assuming appropriate adjustments to monetary policy over time.	13	1
201509	1981	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	That said, we can’t say with certainty what those adjustments will be, as we do not know how foreign economic conditions will evolve, how financial conditions will develop, or how rapidly the remaining domestic headwinds will fade, as recent events amply illustrate.	13	1

201509	1998	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair.	21	2

201509	2000	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As has been the case at each meeting since June, the key issues for your decision today are whether or not the criteria for beginning policy normalization have been met and, in either case, how to communicate in an effective way the reasons for the decision and the Committee’s thinking about the likely response of policy to economic developments going forward.	21	2
201509	2001	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Since you submitted economic projections in June, the incoming information on economic activity and the labor market has been stronger than you anticipated, and the unemployment rate is now lower than you expected—developments that clearly mark further progress on the Committee’s labor market criterion for liftoff.	21	2
201509	2002	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Inflation has continued to run below the Committee’s 2 percent objective, held down importantly by declines in energy prices and prices of non-energy imports.	21	2
201509	2003	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In addition, as discussed earlier, global economic and financial market developments over the intermeeting period have led to a tightening of financial conditions and could pose downside risks to economic activity while putting further downward pressure on inflation in the near term.	21	2
201509	2004	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As summarized on exhibit 1, alternatives A, B, and C provide policy options that reflect differing assessments of the potential effects of recent economic and financial developments on the outlook.	21	2
201509	2005	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Starting with alternative B, paragraph 1 states that “economic activity is expanding at a moderate pace”—in line with the Committee’s previously stated expectations—and indicates that, apart from the continued softness in net exports, the expansion has been somewhat more broadly based than earlier in the year.	21	2
201509	2006	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The paragraph also presents a more confident assessment of the diminution of economic slack than in previous statements, suggesting that, in the Committee’s view, labor market conditions are quite close to meeting the criterion for liftoff.	21	2
201509	2007	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In contrast, it casts recent inflation developments less favorably, suggesting that the effects of the declines in energy prices are not yet behind us and recognizing that market-based measures of inflation compensation have moved lower.	21	2
201509	2008	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 2 continues to describe an outlook in which economic activity will expand at a moderate rate and labor market indicators will move toward mandate- consistent levels.	21	2
201509	2009	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In describing the risks to the outlook, alternative B acknowledges that developments abroad “may restrain [domestic] economic activity somewhat”—a concern that many of you cited in your SEP comments on the outlook.	21	2
201509	2010	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	However, paragraph 2 indicates that, while the Committee is monitoring developments abroad, those developments have not, at this point, tilted the balance of risks to the outlook for economic activity and the labor market appreciably to the downside.	21	2
201509	2011	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Regarding the outlook for inflation, alternative B indicates that recent global developments “are likely to put further downward pressure on inflation in the near term.”	21	2
201509	2012	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	This assessment seems consistent with the fact that many of you have lowered your projections for inflation over the near term as well as with the increase in the number of you who see the risks to inflation to be to the downside.	21	2
201509	2013	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	With this assessment of the outlook for inflation, and the decision to leave the target range for the federal funds rate unchanged, the Committee would convey that it is not yet reasonably confident about its expectation that inflation will move back to 2 percent over the medium term.	21	2
201509	2014	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As summarized in the middle panel, the Committee’s characterization of the recent information on economic activity and the labor market in alternative A would be the same as in alternative B.	21	2
201509	2015	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Nonetheless, its description of recent inflation developments would show greater concern, and it would indicate that recent global developments have shifted the risks to the outlook for economic activity to the downside and will impose some additional restraint on inflation.	21	2
201509	2016	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As a result, the Committee would signal that it does not expect to begin normalizing policy for some time.	21	2
201509	2017	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Moreover, alternative A states that if the Committee did not “soon” see incoming information indicating “that inflation is beginning to move back toward 2 percent,” the Committee would provide additional accommodation to achieve that goal within one to two years.	21	2
201509	2018	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As indicated in the lower panel, alternative C would begin normalizing the level of the federal funds rate.	21	2
201509	2019	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In summarizing the economic background for such a decision, paragraph 1 offers the perspective that economic growth has been moderate, on average, so far this year, and, after citing some key factors showing further improvement in the labor market, it states more definitively that resource slack has diminished.	21	2
201509	2020	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 2 provides further support for the assessment that labor market conditions have met the criterion for liftoff by indicating that labor market indicators are “approaching” mandate-consistent levels.	21	2
201509	2021	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In evaluating the risks to this outlook, the Committee would acknowledge the need to monitor developments abroad but would not suggest that those developments are likely to be consequential for the United States, or that they have altered the Committee’s assessment of risks to the outlook.	21	2
201509	2022	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In alternative C, the Committee would also state that, although inflation is anticipated to remain low over the near term, policymakers have gained sufficient confidence that inflation will move back to 2 percent over the medium run to begin to remove policy accommodation.	21	2
201509	2023	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In paragraph 2, the Committee would state its assessment that the transitory factors holding down inflation “will dissipate,” and that the key determinants of the inflation outlook—continuing improvement in the labor market and stable longer-term expectations—are in place.	21	2
201509	2024	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	I should note that even if you view the policy choice in alternative C to be premature in the present circumstances, you may want to comment on whether paragraph 4 should include the bracketed “balanced approach” language that you discussed at the July meeting.	21	2
