201509	2026	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Your second exhibit reviews market and participants’ monetary policy expectations and some factors likely to shape the market reaction to statements like in the drafts for alternative B or C.	21	2
201509	2027	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As shown in the top-left panel, market participants’ assessment of the probability of a September liftoff, as derived from federal funds futures, varied significantly over the intermeeting period, as Simon already mentioned.	21	2
201509	2028	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The probability appeared to respond to the turbulence in global financial markets, policymaker communications, and incoming economic data.	21	2
201509	2029	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The probability distribution of the timing of liftoff derived from the responses to the Desk’s latest Survey of Primary Dealers—shown to the right—suggests that the perceived odds of policy firming at this meeting are slightly less than 30 percent.	21	2
201509	2030	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As shown by the table in the middle-left panel, although federal funds futures imply notably lower perceived odds of an imminent rate hike than was the case a day before the 1994 and 2004 tightening moves, they still indicate significantly higher odds than were attached to liftoff right before the June meeting.	21	2

201509	2032	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Market participants, on average, place fairly similar odds on liftoff this week, later this year, and next year, as indicated by the fairly uniform distribution of the blue bars in the upper-right panel across the September, December, and later meetings.	21	2

201509	2034	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	However, even among respondents who selected September as the most likely date of liftoff, the median probability attached to a September liftoff was only about 50 percent.	21	2
201509	2035	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	This fact highlights that, indeed, many of them do not seem to hold strong convictions about any one given date.	21	2
201509	2036	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Moreover, as shown in the middle-right panel, views are considerably dispersed.	21	2
201509	2037	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As the distribution of the dots in the leftmost column shows, respondents to the Desk’s surveys of primary dealers and market participants report probabilities for a rate increase at this meeting that range from zero to 60 percent, and the degree of dispersion is similarly high for the December and March meetings.	21	2
201509	2038	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In sum, the current state of market expectations seems consistent with your communications that have for some time emphasized data dependence and, in light of the mixed signals coming from the labor market and inflation, created optionality for when to move.	21	2
201509	2039	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	At the same time, as discussed in the bottom-left panel, whether or not the FOMC decides to raise the target federal funds rate, there could be a revision in investors’ policy expectations that may result in a noticeable market reaction—and one that is hard to predict.	21	2
201509	2040	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	A key point, however, is that the overall market response will be shaped not only by the decision about whether to lift off, but also by the Committee’s communications, including the language in the statement, its economic projections, and the SEP dots.	21	2
201509	2041	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The dots, in particular, indicate that your outlook has not changed materially.	21	2
201509	2042	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The path of the federal funds rate based on the median projection in the SEP, shown in the bottom-right panel, not only remains fairly shallow, but also has shifted down a bit.	21	2
201509	2043	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Such a shallow path might diminish the risk of an outsized market reaction to a statement like alternative C because it conveys the Committee’s intentions to continue to provide a high degree of accommodation for some time.	21	2
201509	2044	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Similarly, as your projections of the federal funds rate continue to indicate that many of you see policy normalization likely to begin later this year, a draft statement like alternative B might be read as clearly keeping interest rate increases later in the year on the table and need not lead to a significant change in the expected path of policy.	21	2
201509	2045	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Having said so, as noted back in the bottom-left panel, there are certainly some risk factors that might trigger an outsized response, especially when you decide to first raise the target range.	21	2
201509	2046	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The fact that longer-term Treasury term premiums are on the low end of their historical range raises the possibility that, after years of the federal funds rate at its effective lower bound, the first rate hike may trigger an abrupt rise in term premiums toward more typical levels, as witnessed during the taper tantrum.	21	2
201509	2047	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In addition, technical factors and market dynamics could play an important role in amplifying movements in interest rates, as witnessed during the taper tantrum.	21	2
201509	2048	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	If investors were to unwind positions abruptly in response to a monetary policy surprise, this could amplify interest rate movements.	21	2
201509	2049	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair.	21	2
201509	2050	2015-09-17	meeting	LAUBACH	That completes my prepared remarks, and I’ll be happy to take questions.	21	2

201509	2101	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Does anyone have other questions for Thomas?	22	2
201509	2102	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Okay.	22	2
201509	2103	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Seeing none, with your indulgence, I would like to start off today’s policy go-round by recommending to the Committee that we adopt alternative B and keep the federal funds rate target range unchanged.	23	2
201509	2104	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Let me explain the basis for this recommendation.	23	2
201509	2105	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I recognize that a good case can be made for moving today.	23	2
201509	2106	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The data that we’ve received since our July meeting on the labor market and domestic spending have been strong, arguably stronger than we expected.	23	2
201509	2107	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Domestic spending appears to be on a solid course, and the labor market has continued to improve, with the unemployment rate declining into the central tendency of the longer-run normal rate of unemployment.	23	2
201509	2108	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	There may well be enough domestic momentum to overcome the slightly greater-than- anticipated drag due to the behavior of the external sector and the tightening of financial conditions.	23	2
201509	2109	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Inflation is way below our target, but there’s no news there.	23	2
201509	2110	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We expected that to be the case.	23	2
201509	2111	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	A significant portion of that shortfall is due to transitory factors, particularly oil prices and the dollar.	23	2
201509	2112	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Although core inflation, even abstracting from the depressing effect of import prices, is running below our objective, with the labor market continuing to improve and survey measures of inflation expectations remaining stable, we should eventually see upward pressure on inflation, returning it to target.	23	2
201509	2113	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	There are lags in the effect of policy, so we need to move in a timely fashion to avoid overshooting our 2 percent objective.	23	2
201509	2114	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	In terms of communications, we’ve prepared the markets for the beginning of normalization later this year.	23	2
201509	2115	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We’ve consistently argued that the significance of a decision to make a small upward adjustment in the funds rate range should not be overblown.	23	2
201509	2116	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	What matters is the path of the funds rate, and we’ve said that we see good reasons why that path is likely to be shallow.	23	2
201509	2117	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Conceivably, raising the target range for the funds rate might even boost the confidence of households and businesses, spurring rather than retarding domestic spending, and perhaps the incessant market focus on the timing of liftoff has itself become a source of uncertainty that’s roiling markets and raising volatility.	23	2
201509	2118	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Perhaps our credibility is at stake if we don’t get on with the job.	23	2
201509	2119	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We may seem as though we’re overreacting to market volatility.	23	2
201509	2120	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I see this as the case for raising rates.	23	2
201509	2121	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I also see a case for not raising rates today, however.	23	2
201509	2122	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	And, in the final analysis, I think that case is stronger.	23	2
201509	2123	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Perhaps most important, my judgment that we should stay on hold reflects my assessment of the balance of risks.	23	2
201509	2124	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	In particular, should it turn out that we’ve waited a bit too long to raise rates, thereby raising the odds that inflation overshoots our 2 percent inflation target, or that we’re forced to move rates up less gradually than we’d prefer—I see those risks as less severe than the risks of moving too soon.	23	2
201509	2125	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I do not want to repeat the experience of other central banks that have tried to free themselves of the zero bound prematurely and later had to reverse course, allowing inflation to move lower during the process.	23	2
201509	2126	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I’m also concerned about what we will communicate to markets and the public about our reaction function and our likely future behavior if we move today, at a time when concerns about the global outlook have created uncertainties that have been reflected in the recent market turmoil and after financial conditions have already tightened notably.	23	2
201509	2127	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We’d be moving when additional deflationary pressure from further dollar appreciation and lower oil prices is working to delay at least slightly our likely return to our inflation target and when it’s hard to find evidence of any fear whatsoever in the marketplace of a 1970s-like inflationary spiral or any sense that the FOMC is “behind the curve.”	23	2
201509	2128	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I’m concerned that we will appear to be hell-bent on raising rates, with the consequence that the dollar might rise significantly and market expectations about the likely future policy path could also shift up substantially.	23	2
201509	2129	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The fact that markets attach only around 30 percent odds to a move today heightens this concern.	23	2
201509	2130	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We set out two criteria for raising rates—that we see some further improvement in the labor market, and that we have reasonable confidence that inflation will move back to our 2 percent target over the medium term.	23	2
201509	2131	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	As I said during the economic go-round, we clearly have seen some further improvement in the labor market.	23	2
201509	2132	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	But as I also noted yesterday, incoming data pertaining to the inflation outlook have not, on balance, improved my confidence that inflation will move up to our target over the next few years.	23	2
201509	2133	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The dollar has strengthened yet further during the intermeeting period.	23	2
201509	2134	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Oil prices have moved yet lower.	23	2
201509	2135	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	And, importantly, those initial indications of an acceleration in wages we thought we had seen have disappeared entirely from all of the main national wage and compensation measures.	23	2
201509	2136	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I’ve gone out of my way to insist that wage acceleration not be viewed as a litmus test for raising the funds rate.	23	2
201509	2137	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	But wage trends are not irrelevant to assessing the remaining degree of slack in the labor market, and the absence of any broad-based wage pressures adds to the case that there remains significant labor market slack.	23	2
201509	2138	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	In effect, I see the short-run natural rate of unemployment as considerably lower than my estimate of the longer-run normal unemployment rate.	23	2
201509	2139	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	This means that there is more scope for improvement in the labor market before inflation pressures emerge, and I see no penalty in allowing the unemployment rate to drift below its estimated longer-run normal value if such an outcome has no adverse implications for inflation.	23	2
201509	2140	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I’d ask you to recall simulations in past Tealbooks of an optimal control path that attaches no weight to unemployment outcomes—it weights only inflation outcomes.	23	2
201509	2141	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Those simulations of an optimal control path tell us that we should be acting more aggressively, pushing unemployment down well below its longer-run normal level.	23	2
201509	2142	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	And the benefit would be that we would promote a more rapid return of inflation to 2 percent.	23	2
201509	2143	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Indeed, this is a reason why I think it makes sense to continue setting as a condition for a first increase in the federal funds rate that we see some further improvement in the labor market.	23	2
201509	2144	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Lastly, I’d note that inflation breakevens have moved yet lower, significantly lower.	23	2
201509	2145	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Despite all of the familiar reasons, this isn’t a definitive indication that inflation expectations have moved down, but it’s certainly disquieting.	23	2
201509	2146	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	While the decline in inflation compensation may not reflect any change in the modal outlook for inflation, I think it plausible that at least a portion of the decline reflects increasing downside risks to inflation.	23	2
201509	2147	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	After all, market participants are increasingly concerned about the global outlook.	23	2
201509	2148	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	They appear to perceive the equilibrium real rate as quite low.	23	2
201509	2149	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	And, with the funds rate at the zero bound and inflation already well below our target, they likely worry that the Fed will have very little ammunition to respond to negative shocks.	23	2
201509	2150	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	This means that inflation could easily fall short of the target in coming years.	23	2
201509	2151	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I share these concerns, and that’s an important reason, I believe, that the risks around our projection that inflation will return to 2 percent are unbalanced to the downside.	23	2
201509	2152	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, the tighter the labor market becomes, the more balanced the risks also become.	23	2
201509	2153	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	There are additional reasons to hold off raising rates today.	23	2
201509	2154	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	They pertain to the global outlook and the fact that overall financial conditions have tightened materially in recent weeks.	23	2
201509	2155	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	As we discussed yesterday, risks to the global outlook have certainly increased.	23	2
201509	2156	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The continuing decline in commodity prices is restraining growth in a number of countries that are commodity exporters.	23	2
201509	2157	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Two of our most important trading partners, Mexico and Canada, have been significantly affected.	23	2
201509	2158	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The prospects, as we discussed, for Chinese growth are highly uncertain, with rising downside risks.	23	2
201509	2159	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Net exports placed a considerable drag on US growth during the first half of the year, and we could see a yet greater effect.	23	2
201509	2160	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	In addition, I’m concerned that we could see significant further appreciation of the dollar.	23	2
201509	2161	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thus, I believe it would be prudent to have some additional information to inform our evaluation of the global outlook before raising rates.	23	2
201509	2162	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Finally, we have seen a material tightening in financial conditions in recent weeks, with US equity prices down and the value of the broad dollar and risk spreads higher.	23	2
201509	2163	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We must always be careful not to allow monetary policy to respond to volatility in the markets.	23	2
201509	2164	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	But the shifts we have seen represent a material tightening in overall financial conditions.	23	2
201509	2165	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Not surprisingly, recent indicators of consumer confidence have retreated somewhat.	23	2
201509	2166	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	It’s conceivable that markets will rebound in the coming weeks and the perceived risks to the global outlook may subside.	23	2
201509	2167	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	If so, a failure to move today will not leave us far behind the curve, if at all.	23	2
201509	2168	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	So my recommendation to the Committee is that we not raise rates today, and that we explain that decision by highlighting that global economic and financial developments have imparted some restraint to the economic outlook and have placed further transitory downward pressure on inflation.	23	2
201509	2169	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We would explain that we have seen continued improvement in the labor market and gained greater confidence about the outlook for domestic spending.	23	2
201509	2170	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	The US economy in that important sense is doing well, but we want to wait for some additional evidence, which could include further improvement in the labor market, to bolster our confidence that inflation will rise to 2 percent in the medium term.	23	2
201509	2171	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We would also emphasize that, despite these recent developments, we have not fundamentally altered our outlook, and that an initial increase in the federal funds rate is a real possibility later this year and what most participants still expect.	23	2
201509	2172	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	I believe communications along these lines would be entirely consistent with the criteria we’ve established for an initial hike in the funds rate and with sensible risk-management considerations.	23	2
201509	2173	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there, and we’ll continue our go-round.	23	2
201509	2174	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We’ll start with President Lacker.	23	2
201509	2175	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2176	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I think now’s the time to raise the federal funds rate target.	23	2
201509	2177	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I’ve felt this way for some time, as you all know, but I haven’t been hell-bent on dissenting.	23	2
201509	2178	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I’ll be listening to this morning’s discussion with great interest, but, at this point, my sense is that it’s going to be difficult to persuade me to support further delay.	23	2
201509	2179	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Our decisions about policy are inevitably decisions about the appropriate level of the short-term real interest rate.	23	2
201509	2180	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	There are a number of approaches to assessing the appropriate real rate, but I’ll start with consumption growth.	23	2
201509	2181	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Basic economic theory tells us that a sustained increase in consumption growth should be associated with higher real interest rates.	23	2
201509	2182	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Granted, this connection isn’t always tight in the data, but the underlying reasoning strongly suggests that a negative 1.2 percent real interest rate is unlikely to be appropriate for an economy with persistent consumption growth at the rate we’ve been seeing.	23	2
201509	2183	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Now, admittedly, there are good arguments for why today’s short-term real interest rate should be lower than historical norms, and these include the global savings glut, an increase in demand for safe assets in the wake of this financial crisis, and ongoing caution on the part of American households.	23	2
201509	2184	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Indeed, a range of attempts at quantification yield measures of the natural real interest rate that are relatively low by historical standards, yet all of these estimates are markedly higher than the actual current level of the real federal funds rate of negative 1.2 percent as reported in the Tealbook.	23	2
201509	2185	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The Laubach-Williams estimate that we’ve been discussing in the past couple of meetings is approximately zero right now—minus 0.1 percent.	23	2
201509	2186	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Economists at the Federal Reserve Bank of Richmond have developed an alternative approach to the Laubach-Williams exercise, one that’s somewhat more agnostic about identifying assumptions and yields an estimate of 0.72 percent.	23	2
201509	2187	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	But the error bands encompass the Laubach-Williams figure, so it’s a very similar estimate.	23	2
201509	2188	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The Tealbook’s estimate of what they call the longer-run funds rate is 1.25 percent, and this is what’s used in the Taylor rule implementations that they report on in Tealbook B.	23	2
201509	2189	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The Tealbook’s FRB/US-model-based estimate of what they call the equilibrium real funds rate is now positive 0.47 percent.	23	2
201509	2190	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Taking any one of these measures as a guide, short-term real interest rates are too low now.	23	2
201509	2191	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Taken together, I think they argue strongly for a rate increase.	23	2
201509	2192	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	A related and complementary approach to assessing interest rate policy is to compare current interest rate settings with patterns of behavior that have been successful for us in the past.	23	2
201509	2193	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The standard approach to summarizing our past behavior is through algebraic policy rule formulas, such as the various versions of the Taylor rule.	23	2
201509	2194	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Tealbook B, as I said, lists the predictions of several of these, and all but one now support raising the nominal funds rate.	23	2
201509	2195	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The one that does not support an increase in rates is the first-difference rule, which, in a sense, is predicated on the assumption that a zero federal funds rate was appropriate last quarter, an assumption that is by no means obvious.	23	2
201509	2196	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The intercept in a Taylor rule is often identified with the natural rate of interest, and some argue that if the natural rate has declined, we should make a corresponding downward adjustment to the prescriptions of those rules.	23	2
201509	2197	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	I point out, however, that the Tealbook already uses a lower natural interest rate assumption than it used to.	23	2
201509	2198	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Now it’s at 1¼ percent in the way it implements those rules.	23	2
201509	2199	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	One would have to argue for a natural interest rate that’s far lower than the estimates I cited—implausibly lower, I might argue—in order to rationalize the current real federal funds rate in the usual Taylor (1993) or Taylor (1999) rule as well as in the inertial Taylor (1999) rule.	23	2
201509	2200	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Of course, one should be wary of using any of these Taylor rules to dictate how to behave at any one meeting.	23	2
201509	2201	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	However, I think the consistent story they tell reinforces the view that the time has come to raise rates.	23	2
201509	2202	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The historical pattern of behavior that’s encapsulated in these rules has delivered generally good outcomes over the past several decades and has conditioned public beliefs about how we’re likely to behave in the future.	23	2
201509	2203	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Such beliefs provide essential foundational support for the monetary stability that we currently enjoy, and we should not take this stability for granted.	23	2
201509	2204	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	If we were to continue to delay, we would be departing even further from the pattern of behavior that has served us well in the past.	23	2
201509	2205	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The historical record strongly suggests that such departures are risky and raise the likelihood of bad outcomes.	23	2
201509	2206	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	In particular, the most damaging departures have been associated with the pursuit of estimates of full-employment unemployment rates that proved, in hindsight, to be too optimistic.	23	2
201509	2207	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The prospect of inflationary risks may seem remote right now.	23	2
201509	2208	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	“Disinflationary pressures” appears to be the catch phrase of the day.	23	2
201509	2209	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	We should remember, however, that the economic outlook can change rapidly.	23	2
201509	2210	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	In mid-2003, for example, falling core inflation evoked a state of high anxiety.	23	2
201509	2211	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	But just over half a year later, growth and inflation were rising, and the need for tighter policy became clear.	23	2
201509	2212	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	In hindsight, we moved too late and too little in that episode as well.	23	2
201509	2213	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	One might reply that because conditions might change, why not just wait and see?	23	2
201509	2214	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	That strategy often seems attractive, particularly when financial market volatility appears to have increased uncertainty.	23	2
201509	2215	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Waiting for the resolution of uncertainty can be a trap, however.	23	2
201509	2216	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	There’s always something new around the corner about which one could be uncertain, or, to quote Governor Fischer quoting a former colleague of his, “It’s never clear next time.	23	2
201509	2217	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	It’s just unclear in a different way.”	23	2
201509	2218	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	As I noted yesterday, we have a history of letting financial market developments affect our policy in ways that we later regret, and we should be mindful of this.	23	2
201509	2219	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	The deeper response is that we know that policy affects the economy with lags, so we should strive to position ourselves in a way that balances future risks.	23	2
201509	2220	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Those risks have been shifting steadily over time as household spending has accelerated and labor market conditions have tightened.	23	2
201509	2221	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Growth in this expansion may have been disappointing when compared with historical averages, but not so much when compared with currently realistic assessments of our capabilities, given productivity and population trends.	23	2
201509	2222	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	In fact, US economic conditions have improved quite significantly over the past six years, all things considered.	23	2
201509	2223	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	It’s time to recognize the substantial progress that’s been achieved and align rates accordingly.	23	2
201509	2224	2015-09-17	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2225	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201509	2226	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Lockhart.	23	2
201509	2227	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2228	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Although I think the policy decision at this meeting is a close and difficult call, I support the policy decision in alternative B.	23	2
201509	2229	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I will also support the statement as written.	23	2
201509	2230	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I have sympathy for Chair Yellen regarding the challenge, even the danger, associated with significant editing of the statement on the fly, particularly just before a press conference.	23	2
201509	2231	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	So I will not suggest any changes, even though I think the statement, and the Committee’s communications more generally, may fall short of what’s needed—a point that I’ll get to in a moment.	23	2
201509	2232	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	By the standard of some further improvement in the labor market, I believe liftoff is justified.	23	2
201509	2233	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	At the same time, I do accept that the inflation data on their face could discourage a liftoff decision at this meeting.	23	2
201509	2234	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The combination of declining year-over-year core PCE inflation and weakening market-based expectation measures is troubling.	23	2
201509	2235	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Nonetheless, I was prepared to look through the inflation data and base a liftoff decision on an assumption, obviously a critical assumption, that the positive forces at work in the economy will eventually result in upward inflation pressures pushing us toward target in a reasonable time frame.	23	2
201509	2236	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Why not lift off with the decision at this meeting?	23	2
201509	2237	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	As I stated in the economic go-round, recent global economic and financial developments have raised the risk to the outlook, in my estimation, and present a challenging environment for executing liftoff.	23	2
201509	2238	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This is the deciding factor for me.	23	2
201509	2239	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The uncertainties that are the likely cause of the recent market volatility justify delaying liftoff a meeting or two.	23	2
201509	2240	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	A delay would give the Committee time to gain confidence that the real economy is not being derailed by these developments.	23	2
201509	2241	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Let me turn to post-statement communication of an alternative B decision and communication in general.	23	2
201509	2242	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I increasingly feel the statement, and our approach to communication more generally, requires a rethink as we approach the next couple of meetings.	23	2
201509	2243	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Said differently, I’m concerned about our approach to forward guidance, and I’d like to offer some thoughts in that regard.	23	2
201509	2244	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m concerned the Committee’s communication has contributed and is contributing to market volatility.	23	2
201509	2245	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m concerned we have allowed our mantra of “data dependence” to become a liability.	23	2
201509	2246	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The shift from strict time-dependent guidance to a more flexible approach based on economic conditionality was appropriate.	23	2
201509	2247	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Over the past several months, however, data dependence has become, effectively, the barest-minimum practical guidance.	23	2
201509	2248	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The phrase provides too little basis for the public to grasp what will drive the Committee’s decisions in the near future.	23	2
201509	2249	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I perceive the need for an attempt to achieve greater consensus on what will both trigger liftoff and drive rate decisions of the Committee as we go forward and then find a way to communicate that consensus to the public.	23	2
201509	2250	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My concern is that, without firming up our guidance, we will continue to fall short of providing the needed clarity about our policy intentions.	23	2
201509	2251	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m concerned the guidance status quo will work at cross-purposes with attaining our objectives.	23	2
201509	2252	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	We will continue to foster a guessing game in the markets that could contribute to unsettled conditions.	23	2
201509	2253	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I recognize the impracticality of trying to engineer substantial statement changes in the remainder of this meeting.	23	2
201509	2254	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	To offer something concrete, however, I suggest that in the intermeeting period, building on our answers in our SEP submissions 3(c), the Committee conduct a virtual go-round on options for forward guidance as captured in a variety of statement alternatives.	23	2
201509	2255	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This discussion might also include statement language at liftoff.	23	2
201509	2256	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Again, I will not suggest actual changes to the alternative B statement.	23	2
201509	2257	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	But if asked what, concretely, I have in mind to make guidance more substantive, I would have liked to see, after the first sentence of paragraph 3, something in substance more along these lines:  First, “the Committee is satisfied that there has been sufficient improvement in labor market conditions.”	23	2
201509	2258	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Next, “the Committee expects that, with continued improvement in labor markets and momentum in economic activity more generally, inflation will rise gradually toward 2 percent over the medium term.”	23	2
201509	2259	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Finally, “in making its policy decision at this meeting, the Committee recognized the elevated risks associated with recent economic and financial developments.	23	2
201509	2260	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	When the Committee views these risks to have dissipated—and absent material negative changes in economic conditions—it is prepared to initiate increases in the federal funds rate range.”	23	2
201509	2261	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Because I see an alternative B decision at this meeting as a deferral or a delay, not just a normal course “no decision” in which the Committee holds off for more or better data, I prefer communicating a strong predisposition—with the usual caveats, of course—to lift off at an upcoming meeting.	23	2
201509	2262	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Statement guidance substantively along the lines of what was just suggested would serve this purpose, in my view.	23	2
201509	2263	2015-09-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2264	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Those are very interesting suggestions.	23	2
201509	2265	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	We will follow up.	23	2
201509	2266	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201509	2267	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	23	2
201509	2268	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2269	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In my view, we have met the conditions for liftoff, and I therefore prefer alternative C.	23	2
201509	2270	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	On the employment side of the mandate, we are at or very near full employment.	23	2
201509	2271	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Unemployment is at or within sight of the natural rate.	23	2
201509	2272	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And many other measures of labor market conditions have approached or exceeded their long-run or steady-state values.	23	2
201509	2273	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	This reduction in slack gives me confidence that inflation will return to 2 percent over the next few years.	23	2
201509	2274	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The only reason inflation has not made much progress toward that goal is the offset from the drop in commodity prices and the appreciation of the dollar.	23	2
201509	2275	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	However, these facts will only temporarily depress the inflation rate.	23	2
201509	2276	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Furthermore, alternative measures of inflation, such as the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas’s trimmed mean rate, suggest that underlying inflation is already closer to our objective than some other measures would suggest.	23	2
201509	2277	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In considering the appropriate stance of policy, I start with commonly used benchmarks for monetary policy, such as policy rules and the optimal control simulations.	23	2
201509	2278	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Based on my forecast, nearly all suggest that we should raise rates now or already should have raised rates some time ago.	23	2
201509	2279	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But that’s just a starting point for thinking about policy, and there are valid arguments for delay and continuing to err on the side of caution relative to these benchmarks.	23	2
201509	2280	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	First, the zero bound remains a constraint on our ability to deal with adverse shocks.	23	2
201509	2281	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’ve already done a great deal of keeping rates lower for longer, but this remains a concern.	23	2
201509	2282	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Second, there are some notable downside risks at present, as many people mentioned, including further dollar appreciation and concerns about growth abroad.	23	2
201509	2283	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Finally, inflation has been running below target for quite some time, and a low-inflation environment remains in effect around the globe.	23	2
201509	2284	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	There are also compelling arguments in favor of moving sooner rather than later, however.	23	2
201509	2285	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	First, the long lags of monetary policy require taking out some insurance against the possibility that the high-pressure economy in train for next year will boil over.	23	2
201509	2286	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We do not have the luxury of delaying liftoff until we’ve reached or exceeded both of our policy targets.	23	2
201509	2287	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	At that point, we’d be hopelessly behind the curve.	23	2
201509	2288	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Second, there are some upside risks to our outlook that balance the downside ones.	23	2
201509	2289	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Lower oil prices haven’t yet sparked a surge in consumption, but that may change as households start interpreting the decline as more permanent.	23	2
201509	2290	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Housing starts, which remain well below historical averages, could also surprise on the upside.	23	2
201509	2291	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Finally, I’m concerned that, by staying at the zero bound for too long, we may be creating new economic and financial imbalances.	23	2
201509	2292	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Although these risks appear contained for the present, we already have elevated price-dividend ratios in equity markets, high and growing house-price- to-rent ratios, continued capital movements into emerging market economies, and other riskier investment vehicles that could become problematic.	23	2
201509	2293	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Further delay in raising rates will incite additional search for yield and exacerbate our exposure to costly reversals.	23	2
201509	2294	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	At this point, I want to respond to President Kocherlakota’s question about what it means to boil over.	23	2
201509	2295	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I’m going to go back to June 2005, when I was one of the briefers of the FOMC.	23	2
201509	2296	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We were talking about the housing bubble.	23	2
201509	2297	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	You may disagree with the word “bubble,” but house prices were very elevated in June 2005.	23	2
201509	2298	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	There was a discussion of what that meant for the economy, and I was one of the presenters as a member of the staff of the Federal Reserve Bank of San Francisco.	23	2
201509	2299	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I remember then Vice Chairman Geithner asking me during a break, “What do we do about it now?	23	2
201509	2300	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s mid-2005.	23	2
201509	2301	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	House prices are, by our own estimates, 25 or 30 percent overvalued.	23	2
201509	2302	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is already in place.	23	2
201509	2303	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Do we raise interest rates and prick the bubble?	23	2
201509	2304	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Or do we wait around and clean up?”	23	2
201509	2305	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, it’s important to remember that this was not in the context of a financial crisis— that’s not what we were worried about at the time.	23	2
201509	2306	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That was perhaps a mistake.	23	2
201509	2307	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We were worried about what would happen if house prices fell 20, 25, or 30 percent, and then about what effect that would have on the economy, just from purely macroeconomic concerns.	23	2
201509	2308	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	What I realized personally in that sidebar conversation was, I didn’t actually have a good answer.	23	2
201509	2309	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Once the overvaluation of house prices had already occurred, we didn’t have good options regarding how to reduce these imbalances.	23	2
201509	2310	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Raising interest rates sharply would create, clearly, huge negative repercussions and probably would accelerate the decline in the housing market, which was unsustainable.	23	2
201509	2311	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Waiting around to see what happens and clean up afterward obviously wasn’t a good answer.	23	2
201509	2312	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I came away from the conversation thinking about that for the past 10 years, and I realized, you know, the time to have that conversation was in 2002 and 2003.	23	2
201509	2313	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That’s when we first saw signs that things were getting out of whack—concerns about and risks to the economy were rising.	23	2
201509	2314	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And thinking about where the tradeoffs really were at that point—not being driven by housing or stock market bubbles, because we went through this in the 1990s, too, but really weighing what the costs are of seeing how far this economy will go and taking into consideration those risks before they actually become problematic.	23	2
201509	2315	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Let me put that in context.	23	2
201509	2316	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Today, according to a standard measure, the house-price-to- rent ratio is about 30 percent above historical norms.	23	2
201509	2317	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We can disagree about what the average level is—and the Board’s staff has its own views on this—but if you take historical norms between 1980 and 2000, the standard price-to-rent ratio is about where we were in 2003.	23	2
201509	2318	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And house prices are rising very dramatically today.	23	2
201509	2319	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, I’m not talking about a financial crisis, because regarding our bank supervision and financial stability, I think we’re in a situation that’s 10 times better.	23	2
201509	2320	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of macroeconomic risk—the risk that, a couple of years from now, we’ll be in a situation in which the economy is threatened, whether by asset prices in general or other imbalances—I believe there are real concerns.	23	2
201509	2321	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I don’t want to get into the position, once we’re in the situation that we faced 10 years ago, of having to ask, “Well, what do we do now?”	23	2
201509	2322	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the past, I’ve weighed these pros and cons and come down on the side of delaying liftoff.	23	2
201509	2323	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But the ongoing improvement in the labor market and the general economy has tilted the balance of these arguments in favor of raising rates sooner rather than later.	23	2
201509	2324	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I therefore believe that a rate increase today will be the best policy choice.	23	2
201509	2325	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That said, I recognize that it is a close call, and I did listen very carefully, Chair Yellen, to your weighing of these issues.	23	2
201509	2326	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Obviously, a different weighting of the pros and cons that you described may lead one to prefer delaying liftoff until the next meeting or even the one thereafter.	23	2
201509	2327	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	As such, I’m willing to be patient and support alternative B today as written.	23	2
201509	2328	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	However, I do think it is important, picking up on the comments of President Lockhart, that we do keep all future meetings live, including October.	23	2
201509	2329	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	If developments between now and then argue for liftoff, we should be ready to take that action, call a press conference, and provide an opportunity for the Chair to explain our decision at that time.	23	2
201509	2330	2015-09-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you.	23	2
201509	2331	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201509	2332	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	23	2
201509	2333	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2334	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I support alternative B.	23	2
201509	2335	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I did not view this decision today as a close call.	23	2
201509	2336	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	With little time to process recent financial market movements and international concerns, we need more time to understand whether there’s been a more significant underlying change in economic fundamentals.	23	2
201509	2337	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The first footnote in Tealbook A makes clear that the economic effect of delaying a tightening by a meeting or two would have a de minimis effect on variables we care about.	23	2
201509	2338	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Tightening at this meeting, with excessive volatility and using new tools to get us off the zero lower bound, risks a much more complicated start to our tightening cycle.	23	2
201509	2339	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It also risks the possibility of tightening at the start of a more significant global slowdown, which is not in my modal forecast but is now a more elevated risk.	23	2
201509	2340	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Reasonable risk management leads me to want to see more data before acting.	23	2
201509	2341	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	That said, I do view the time to raise rates as being near.	23	2
201509	2342	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	While the U-3 unemployment rate is not a sufficient statistic to summarize labor market conditions, it also should not be ignored.	23	2
201509	2343	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Employment growth has been pretty strong this year, and broader measures of slack—	23	2
201509	2344	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	U-4, U-5, and U-6—have also improved significantly.	23	2
201509	2345	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	As we’ve underestimated how quickly unemployment rates would decline, it is possible that we will face much tighter labor markets sooner than I have in my forecast.	23	2
201509	2346	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If that were to happen, I would expect less delay in reaching our inflation target.	23	2
201509	2347	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In light of the recent market volatility and the uncertainty about the inflation forecast, I would prefer that our tightening, whenever it begins, be quite gradual.	23	2
201509	2348	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	A risk to waiting too long to lift off is that we may need to tighten more quickly than is in my SEP forecast.	23	2
201509	2349	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, waiting until next year risks a more pronounced decline in unemployment than is in my modal forecast and a more rapid return to 2 percent inflation than we currently envision.	23	2
201509	2350	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Under those conditions, we would be caught behind the curve and need to make a more rapid adjustment to policy.	23	2
201509	2351	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I’d prefer to avoid such a circumstance.	23	2
201509	2352	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would like each of the meetings, whether they coincide with an SEP release and a planned press conference, to be live.	23	2
201509	2353	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If the domestic and global economy is slowing down, there will be no need to tighten.	23	2
201509	2354	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, if labor markets continue to improve and the recent financial market turbulence does not leave much trace in the data going forward, it seems prudent to me to begin a gradual tightening process relatively soon.	23	2
201509	2355	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I have a couple of quick comments on the reinvestment discussion.	23	2
201509	2356	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I didn’t comment yesterday because I wanted to process people’s comments.	23	2
201509	2357	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I had a couple of quick takeaways.	23	2
201509	2358	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	First, when we don’t know what we will do, I don’t think we should provide forward guidance.	23	2
201509	2359	2015-09-17	meeting		[Laughter]	23	2
201509	2360	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I disagree.	23	2
201509	2361	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	[Laughter]	23	2
201509	2362	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I can imagine a scenario in which we actually sell long-term assets.	23	2
201509	2363	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is the tabletop scenario, where we meet our dual-mandate goals but commercial real estate and residential real estate are in a bubble, somewhat like what President Williams was talking about.	23	2
201509	2364	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In that case, I would certainly consider selling long-term assets, with the very purpose of steepening the yield curve.	23	2
201509	2365	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I can also imagine a scenario in which we maintain a large balance sheet.	23	2
201509	2366	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If the equilibrium real federal funds rate is low, we may want to keep long rates low and short rates higher than otherwise to minimize the chance that we return to the zero lower bound.	23	2
201509	2367	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It has been costly to be at the zero lower bound.	23	2
201509	2368	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would prefer to minimize the chance that we return there.	23	2
201509	2369	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we are not willing to raise our inflation target, we should consider maintaining a higher balance sheet.	23	2
201509	2370	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The discussion yesterday was very good but implied to me that we should maintain balance sheet flexibility as prudent risk management.	23	2
201509	2371	2015-09-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201509	2373	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	23	2
201509	2374	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2375	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I support alternative C for today.	23	2
201509	2376	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In paragraph 4, I support adding the bracketed “balanced approach” language.	23	2
201509	2377	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In paragraph 5, I suggest using the language in the bracketed choice “at least during the early stages of normalization.”	23	2
201509	2378	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I remain very concerned that a decision at this meeting to adopt alternative B will essentially cement the idea of a “Yellen put” in the eyes of financial markets.	23	2
201509	2379	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The added language in alternative B, paragraph 2, basically says that the global selloff during the intermeeting period is our basis for nonaction.	23	2
201509	2380	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	No amount of explaining will disguise this fact.	23	2
201509	2381	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The message will be lost on no one.	23	2
201509	2382	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I think we’re kidding ourselves about what this means for the future of the Committee.	23	2
201509	2383	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The problem with this is that it will create questions as to how the Committee will react to future selloffs or booms in financial markets.	23	2
201509	2384	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Many argued yesterday that the implications for US growth and inflation, not the global financial turmoil, were the key determinants of this decision.	23	2
201509	2385	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	However, most of the weak spots around the world have been well known—Brazil and Russia were cited yesterday—and were widely discussed at previous meetings.	23	2
201509	2386	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The Chinese devaluation was indeed a surprise to markets during the intermeeting period, but it was not a big enough event to have a meaningful impact on US monetary policy strategy.	23	2
201509	2387	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Chinese growth is, indeed, slowing and will continue to slow in coming years, but this has been well known for some time and hardly qualifies as news.	23	2
201509	2388	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The evidence of an actual hard landing in China is very limited, and our own staff assessment is that such a scenario is unlikely, on the basis of the data available today.	23	2
201509	2389	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In a nutshell, we are making a decision today that emphasizes vague, unspecified, and likely quantitatively small effects on the US economy emanating from the RMB depreciation decision.	23	2
201509	2390	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	This is not a good basis for US monetary policy strategy.	23	2
201509	2391	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Some are claiming that global commodity price declines are the driving factor here, but, on balance, this is a bullish factor for the United States, not a bearish factor.	23	2
201509	2392	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	One of my concerns is that we are sending a very muddled message about our reaction function.	23	2
201509	2393	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	We have in many ways become very discretionary in our policy choices, citing different factors on different days, even when the general nature of the economic situation has not changed appreciably.	23	2
201509	2394	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Concerning inflation, I’m delighted to learn that there’s been a sudden shift in sentiment on the Committee toward strict inflation targeting—that is, running monetary policy with heavy emphasis on inflation and little or no emphasis on output or employment gaps.	23	2
201509	2395	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I actually think this would be a reasonable way to proceed and could lead to reasonably good policy in the United States, but it has not enjoyed as much popularity in the past as it has recently.	23	2
201509	2396	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	However, there is a problem with what I’m calling strict inflation-targeting approaches in the current circumstances.	23	2
201509	2397	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Strict inflation targeting says that the reason we are still at the zero lower bound is that inflation is below target.	23	2
201509	2398	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	This would be a good reason to be at perhaps a 2 percent policy rate, still well below long-run normal levels.	23	2
201509	2399	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	But it is not a good reason to be near zero on the policy rate, 350 basis points below normal levels.	23	2
201509	2400	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	That suggests a very high elasticity of the federal funds rate to the inflation gap.	23	2
201509	2401	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In other words, a relatively small inflation gap implies a lot of accommodation—a 0 percent federal funds rate.	23	2
201509	2402	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	What that means is, as inflation rises, the federal funds rate will, at least if you are taking this approach, rise very quickly, and that is not what the Committee is saying.	23	2
201509	2403	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I agree with Governor Fischer’s assessment from yesterday on the idea that temporary factors are influencing inflation, as many have said around here.	23	2
201509	2404	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	As these abate, a strict inflation-targeting approach would suggest a rapid increase in the policy rate.	23	2
201509	2405	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	We’re evidently not planning to do that, so it’s exactly this process that will lead to perceptions that the Committee is far behind the proverbial curve.	23	2
201509	2406	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I see this as a poor decision today, and I just want to think about what the fallout will be and how the Committee has to manage going forward.	23	2
201509	2407	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Even though I think we’re not making a good decision here, we can make good decisions in the future.	23	2
201509	2408	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	I see four consequences.	23	2
201509	2409	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	First, I think that the Committee will be viewed as shifting to a “late and fast” strategy and away from an “early and gradual” strategy.	23	2
201509	2410	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The perception in markets, which is already there, will be that the Committee will not move until we’re forced into action.	23	2
201509	2411	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	It also suggests that the Committee is perhaps more willing to scramble to catch up, if necessary—or at least that’s the way we’re weighing that risk.	23	2
201509	2412	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Second, this shift toward a late-and-fast strategy, combined with an undefined reaction function, will mean even more volatility in the future due to uncertainty about Fed policy than we would otherwise have.	23	2
201509	2413	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	What we’re saying, essentially, is that when the Committee moves, it may have to move faster.	23	2
201509	2414	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	In addition, it is not that clear what the Committee might react to, because we’re taking a very discretionary approach to our policy and a very eclectic approach to what variables we want to cite in making our policy decision.	23	2
201509	2415	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Third, I think there’s more risk now of an outsized increase in rates at some point in the future, not unlike the moves of 50 or 75 basis points that were made in 1994.	23	2
201509	2416	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	If you’re going to play the late-and-fast strategy, then you’ve got to possibly be ready to move more quickly than I think the Committee is currently ready for.	23	2
201509	2417	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Markets will sense this, and this will create additional uncertainty in financial markets.	23	2
201509	2418	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Finally, I think there will be a continued and exacerbated mismatch between market expectations and FOMC expectations about future policy.	23	2
201509	2419	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee will now put out its SEP.	23	2
201509	2420	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	It will have a policy rate path, but those in the markets that think the Committee will never move will be emboldened to move even further into the future.	23	2
201509	2421	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	So there will be more of a gap now between what the FOMC expects regarding monetary policy and what the market expects.	23	2
201509	2422	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Those gaps can’t persist indefinitely.	23	2
201509	2423	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	They have to be reconciled at some point, and that process leads to additional volatility in markets and is part of what was going on here, I think, during the summer.	23	2
201509	2424	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Those are my four takeaways for the consequences of today’s decision.	23	2
201509	2425	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Again, I support alternative C.	23	2
201509	2426	2015-09-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201509	2428	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Mester.	23	2
201509	2429	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2430	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	I believe there’s a strong case for moving the federal funds rate up at this meeting.	23	2
201509	2431	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	The Committee has laid out two criteria for liftoff—some further improvement in labor markets and reasonable confidence that inflation will move back to our target of 2 percent over the medium term.	23	2
201509	2432	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	In my view, those conditions have been met.	23	2
201509	2433	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Labor market conditions certainly continued to improve over the intermeeting period, and, in my view, the economy is at or nearly at full employment from the standpoint of the Fed’s dual-mandate goal.	23	2
201509	2434	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	The inflation criterion for liftoff is appropriately based on the expected path of inflation and not on its current level.	23	2
201509	2435	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	No doubt inflation has been running below our goal of 2 percent, but the effects of last summer’s oil price decline and fall in import prices have been passing through to the headline inflation numbers.	23	2
201509	2436	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	This, combined with the fact that the labor market has been tightening faster than expected and inflation expectations have been generally stable even in the face of commodity price declines, should give us more confidence in our inflation forecast.	23	2
201509	2437	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Starting normalization before we reach our dual-mandate goals is prudent if we want to minimize the risk that we’ll have to move rates up considerably more aggressively than we’re currently anticipating.	23	2
201509	2438	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	We’ve been indicating for some time that we expect a gradual path.	23	2
201509	2439	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	I would like us to take actions that help maintain the credibility of that scheme.	23	2
201509	2440	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	As Governor Fischer said at our July meeting, the data control the gradualness.	23	2
201509	2441	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	However, our policy actions can influence the data by influencing how the economy evolves.	23	2
201509	2442	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Now, should the recent volatility in financial markets give us pause?	23	2
201509	2443	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	I think not.	23	2
201509	2444	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	The economy has fared well through it.	23	2
201509	2445	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Volatility measures and risk spreads remain elevated but are moving back down.	23	2
201509	2446	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	As Chair Yellen pointed out, the decision to act depends on an assessment of the risks.	23	2
201509	2447	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	I view the change in financial conditions and reassessment of global growth since our July meeting as a downside risk to the outlook rather than implying much change to the modal outlook.	23	2
201509	2448	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	But we’ve taken out insurance against this downside risk by keeping interest rates considerably lower than almost all of the policy rules suggest, even as the Tealbook- consistent equilibrium interest rate has been rising—in this Tealbook it’s now 0.47 percent.	23	2
201509	2449	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	I believe that Chair Yellen’s insightful leadership of the Committee has prepared the public for liftoff.	23	2
201509	2450	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	In the current environment, after keeping the funds rate at zero for over six years, I would expect some residual uncertainty surrounding the decision.	23	2
201509	2451	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	The fact that there’s not unanimity across market participants and forecasters that liftoff will occur at this particular meeting doesn’t deter me.	23	2
201509	2452	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Most are still expecting a rate hike this year, and a resolution of some policy uncertainty might actually be viewed favorably.	23	2
201509	2453	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	In addition, no matter how well we have prepared and signaled such a change, I’d expect some volatility in the markets at liftoff.	23	2
201509	2454	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	I don’t think we should be too bothered by that, either.	23	2
201509	2455	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	What would concern me more is if, on liftoff, the public’s expectation about the path of policy after liftoff changes and becomes much steeper than the path we’re currently anticipating.	23	2
201509	2456	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	In other words, might liftoff be read as the beginning of rate increases at each meeting thereafter so that we have a steep path going up?	23	2
201509	2457	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	The Chair has emphasized that the Committee anticipates that economic conditions will evolve in a way that warrants keeping the funds rate below its longer-run level for some time.	23	2
201509	2458	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	This certainly shows up in our SEP.	23	2
201509	2459	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	But the market path implied by market data is considerably shallower than in the SEP, which suggests that the message of a gradual path is coming through loud and clear.	23	2
201509	2460	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Thus, while there is some risk that the act of liftoff may appreciably change policy expectations, I believe appropriate communications at liftoff will be sufficient to mitigate this risk.	23	2
201509	2461	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Chair Yellen and the Committee have navigated some very difficult waters over the past year, as the start of normalization is near.	23	2
201509	2462	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	With considerable effort, we’ve reached a point at which there is a favorable alignment of expectations of a rate increase and the data that support such an increase.	23	2
201509	2463	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	I don’t believe this is something we should take for granted.	23	2
201509	2464	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Current economic circumstances are very favorable in terms of being able to communicate the rationale for action and post-liftoff policy, and careful communication is a crucial component of a successful liftoff.	23	2
201509	2465	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Yes, there are risks to moving.	23	2
201509	2466	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	But there are also risks to not moving, including having to move more aggressively later on if we delay too much further.	23	2
201509	2467	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Action is going to send a signal, but so will inaction.	23	2
201509	2468	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	We may not see such favorable conditions for communications for some time.	23	2
201509	2469	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Thus, I believe we should seize the day and act.	23	2
201509	2470	2015-09-17	meeting	MESTER	Of course, I do understand that this is not the majority view, and I respect colleagues who see things differently.	23	2

201509	2475	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	Given my economic forecast, I continue to hold the position that it is quite important that monetary policy begin to raise rates.	23	2
201509	2476	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	However, I am not adamant that it be done at this meeting.	23	2
201509	2477	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	The recent turbulence in financial markets and the softening of energy prices and price pressures in general probably make this meeting less than optimal for liftoff, although I expect these are temporary headwinds.	23	2
201509	2478	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	It is, however, my strong belief that we should begin our normalization process sooner rather than later, and that the process should be gradual.	23	2
201509	2479	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	At the least, the statement language should make clear that if we continue to see improvements in the labor market over the next couple of months, the Committee will move to raise rates.	23	2
201509	2480	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	Earlier liftoff makes a gradual path of policy firming more likely, and it will still allow us to maintain an accommodative policy stance for some time.	23	2
201509	2481	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	I’m becoming concerned that we will find ourselves treating every bump in the economic road as a reason for delay, with the effect that monetary policy moves further and further from what can reasonably be viewed as normal.	23	2
201509	2482	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	The longer we wait in anticipation that all signs point in the same direction, the more likely it will be that future policy adjustments will need to be very aggressive, and I worry about the economic consequences of being in that position.	23	2
201509	2483	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	Beginning normalization should send a reassuring message and will underscore the belief that the economy is on solid footing, and that inflation will return to target.	23	2
201509	2484	2015-09-17	meeting	HARKER	It seems that the least normal element of the current economic environment is our inability to return monetary policy to a more normal mode of conduct.	23	2

201509	2488	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Kaplan.	23	2
201509	2489	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2490	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Based on economic data and the outlook for the economy discussed yesterday, I do believe we’re at a point at which it’s appropriate to begin the process of removing accommodation—if not today, then very soon.	23	2
201509	2491	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	I do support alternative B today because I am of the view that economic conditions abroad might have the potential to spill over to the United States, thereby increasing the uncertainty about the US outlook and negatively affecting data in the months ahead.	23	2
201509	2492	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	However, I would say that I believe these non-US economic uncertainties will continue for some extended period.	23	2
201509	2493	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	That is, I don’t believe the overall level of this uncertainty is going to diminish in the coming months.	23	2
201509	2494	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	The nature of the weakness and spillover threats from abroad relates to deeply embedded, in some cases, structural, demographic, and other issues that are likely to take years, versus months, to manage and address.	23	2
201509	2495	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	So my preference would be that we soon begin the process of removing accommodation and address these potential spillover threats by adjusting the expected path of accommodation, versus delaying much further the start of the process.	23	2
201509	2496	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	In my view, delaying for too long the start of the process of removing accommodation at this stage carries a cost.	23	2
201509	2497	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	While a lower unemployment rate, of course, is desirable, it has the potential to create unhealthy imbalances if it’s supported by artificially accommodative financial conditions.	23	2
201509	2498	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Such conditions maintained for too long may encourage investment and borrowing decisions that cannot easily be reversed or unwound when policy eventually normalizes, as it must.	23	2
201509	2499	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	This increases the chances, in my view, of a hard landing, which, to me, means excess investment, inventory buildup, and financial asset valuations that are more likely to lead to negative economic effects later when more normal policy is put into place.	23	2
201509	2500	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	In my experience, imbalances like these are often not obvious until after the fact, and they need not be accompanied by above-target inflation.	23	2
201509	2501	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	So I would say that, on the upside, prudent risk management dictates that we begin the process of scaling back accommodation as the economy approaches our best estimate of potential.	23	2
201509	2502	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	I can and do support alternative B as written at this meeting, though, because I believe that it is prudent to use the next several weeks or months to confirm that conditions for liftoff are sustainable, allowing us to act in October or December.	23	2
201509	2503	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	But I would suggest that, in the statement, we send a signal that the economy has moved closer to satisfying the conditions for liftoff by substituting the word “approaching” for the phrase “continuing to move toward” in the third sentence of paragraph 2 in alternative B.	23	2
201509	2504	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	So, in that third sentence, it currently says “continuing to move toward,” and my suggestion is to instead substitute the word “approaching.”	23	2
201509	2505	2015-09-17	meeting	KAPLAN	Thank you.	23	2
