201509	2519	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Around the world, downside inflation risks abound.	23	2
201509	2520	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Since our June SEP round, the United States has been buffeted by additional disinflationary headwinds from low energy, commodity, and imported goods prices.	23	2
201509	2521	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	In the US, the improvement in the labor market has not yet produced any meaningful signs of wage or cost pressures.	23	2
201509	2522	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	It’s no wonder that none of my business contacts cite any concerns about rising inflationary pressures.	23	2
201509	2523	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	There’s another reason I find it hard to be confident that we are headed to 2 percent inflation at an appropriate pace.	23	2
201509	2524	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I’m referring to what I think must be a concern by many on this Committee about a modest overshooting of our inflation target.	23	2
201509	2525	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Madam Chair, I will say that in my initial prepared remarks here, I had “tacit concern.”	23	2
201509	2526	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But it turns out you were much more explicit in your own concern about overshooting, and I think others have been today as well.	23	2
201509	2527	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I sense that many participants’ SEP forecasts are trying to thread the needle to get to 2 percent without any risk of overshooting.	23	2
201509	2528	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	With inflation so very low, that’s the only way I can rationalize some of our SEP policy rate paths, at least given my outlook.	23	2
201509	2529	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I infer that these paths reflect a serious aversion to PCE inflation heading to, say, 2½ percent.	23	2
201509	2530	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But after six or seven years of inflation averaging 1½ percent, whether we briefly touch 2 percent during that time isn’t really relevant.	23	2
201509	2531	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	And with forecasts for several more years below target, we should be very nervous about advocating policies that seek to eliminate any chance of 2½ percent inflation.	23	2
201509	2532	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Outsized concerns over exceeding 2 percent inflation will risk signaling that our price objective is a ceiling and not a symmetric target.	23	2
201509	2533	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	It also risks us joining other central banks that are struggling with the consequences of not sufficiently defending their inflation objectives from below and of ignoring the added risk emanating from the zero lower bound.	23	2
201509	2534	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Furthermore, I don’t see much risk of inflation running anywhere near 2½ percent over the forecast period.	23	2
201509	2535	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	To the contrary, the inflation risks largely seem to be to the downside.	23	2
201509	2536	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The Tealbook alternative scenarios highlight this.	23	2
201509	2537	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Like President Kocherlakota, I can’t recall the last time every alternative simulation was more pessimistic about inflation than the baseline scenario, which isn’t that optimistic to start with.	23	2
201509	2538	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	From a risk-management perspective, these adverse alternatives suggest there could be significant benefits to delaying any substantial increase in the funds rate in order to build up a buffer stock of inflation pressures.	23	2
201509	2539	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	In turn, such a buffer would reduce the risk of returning to the zero lower bound if these plausible shocks indeed come to pass.	23	2
201509	2540	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Another way to put this is that our policies should allow a higher probability of inflation rising to the range of 2 to 2½ percent for a time.	23	2
201509	2541	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	To achieve a symmetric 2 percent objective in the face of the likely asymmetric policy risks emanating from the nonlinearity of the zero lower bound, we have to allow ourselves a reasonable chance of going above 2 percent.	23	2
201509	2542	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Less bold action could signal that we were content to have PCE inflation settle in at 1.5 to 1.9 percent, the latter being the Tealbook outlook in 2018.	23	2
201509	2543	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	My SEP date for policy liftoff is June 2016.	23	2
201509	2544	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	This is not as extreme as the dot chart might suggest.	23	2
201509	2545	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	After all, my overall funds rate path is not all that different from the implications of the Tealbook’s path.	23	2
201509	2546	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	If things play out as expected, the differences are mainly around near-term timing.	23	2
201509	2547	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	My SEP submission delays liftoff both to build a risk-management buffer and to allow us time to better assess the outlook before making a policy move.	23	2
201509	2548	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	At the end of 2016, I have the funds rate range at 75 to 100 basis points.	23	2
201509	2549	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	From today, that’s a total of three increases of 25 basis points each.	23	2
201509	2550	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	My subsequent path is a touch steeper than the Tealbook’s, so we both arrive at about the same rate by the end of 2018.	23	2
201509	2551	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I believe that lower rates in the near term, followed by a bit faster ascent after we have more confidence in the inflation outlook, would allow for better risk assessment and would be appropriate as long as our inflation outlook is below 2½ percent.	23	2
201509	2552	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Again, the way to get to 2 percent within a reasonable period of time, or at all, is to make sure you give yourself a reasonable chance of getting to 2 percent.	23	2
201509	2553	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Finally, I think our medium-term policy focus should be on communicating our commitment to a 2 percent symmetric PCE inflation objective.	23	2
201509	2554	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Like President Lockhart, I feel that the term “data dependence” hasn’t been sufficient for the public to understand how policy will react to incoming data.	23	2
201509	2555	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	But I believe President Lockhart’s suggestions are limited to clarifying when liftoff will take place.	23	2
201509	2556	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	We need more than that.	23	2
201509	2557	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Providing more information with respect to our funds rate path milestones and how they relate to the inflation outlook would be quite valuable for supporting the achievement of our 2 percent objective.	23	2
201509	2558	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	The SEP dot chart should be helpful on this score if we focus most of our communications on the central portions of the chart.	23	2
201509	2559	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Saying “more gradual than normal” isn’t enough unless we say it a lot.	23	2
201509	2560	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Beyond today, if inflation headwinds continue to challenge our outlook even as we begin liftoff, then I think our communications, especially those discussing data dependence, will need to signal even more aggressively our full commitment to achieving our 2 percent symmetric inflation objective.	23	2
201509	2561	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	I support alternative B.	23	2
201509	2562	2015-09-17	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201509	2564	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	President George.	23	2
201509	2565	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2566	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	Alternative C aligns with my own views of the economy’s continued expansion, even in the face of various headwinds over the past several years—an economy that warrants a continued accommodative stance of policy but not zero interest rates, in my view.	23	2
201509	2567	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	The benchmark policy rules that supported the Committee’s decisions to add accommodation via LSAPs several years ago are the same ones that have been signaling for some time that a shift in policy is appropriate.	23	2
201509	2568	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	However, for a Committee that has lacked reasonable confidence to begin a gradual normalization over the past few meetings, the prospects of liftoff in the face of global growth uncertainty and the related headwinds to the United States are actually less compelling, I think, today.	23	2
201509	2569	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	I understand the desire to wait for a few more meetings, with the intention of having a clearer picture of the outlook.	23	2
201509	2570	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	Waiting for more certainty over the course of a few more meetings may seem comforting and costless.	23	2
201509	2571	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	I think it carries its own cumulative risk.	23	2
201509	2572	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	The potential exists to get caught in a time-inconsistency trap by projecting liftoff in the near future but, when the time comes, lacking the conviction to carry out the policies underpinning our projections because of wanting to see just a few more data points.	23	2
201509	2573	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	I’ll offer three brief thoughts for today’s decision.	23	2
201509	2574	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	First, in view of the continued improvement in labor market conditions, the decision not to lift off at this meeting must surely reflect the Committee as not yet having reasonable confidence that inflation will return to 2 percent over the medium term.	23	2
201509	2575	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	If this point is not emphasized, markets may view our reaction function as now incorporating things like market volatility and foreign developments into our near-term decisionmaking process.	23	2
201509	2576	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	Second, I believe the heavy emphasis on data dependence is injecting substantial uncertainty into markets and is too backward looking.	23	2
201509	2577	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	So, in addition to data dependence, monetary policy needs to emphasize being forward looking.	23	2
201509	2578	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	We should place more emphasis on how incoming data are affecting our assessment of the outlook rather than inadvertently sending a message that we’re responding to the most recent data points.	23	2
201509	2579	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	Finally, postponing liftoff increases the probability that rates will have to be increased more rapidly than we currently anticipate.	23	2
201509	2580	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	Waiting until inflation is nearer to 2 percent and unemployment is below its longer-run normal rate may put the Committee in a difficult position of having to adjust rates more steeply and, as a result, create heightened risk around financial stability and our growth outlook.	23	2
201509	2581	2015-09-17	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you.	23	2

201509	2590	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As President Evans emphasized, those risks really are all asymmetrically on the downside at this stage because of the zero lower bound and our inability to be able to respond effectively to those risks.	23	2
201509	2591	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What I heard from many around the table is a desire to incorporate other considerations besides the outlook into our thinking.	23	2
201509	2592	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	President Lacker started off by talking about how the Taylor rule had given very good outcomes for us in the past.	23	2
201509	2593	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Embedded in the Taylor rule is a sense of the desirability to have interest rates close to their long-run normal level.	23	2
201509	2594	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	President Lockhart talked about being satisfied with gradually moving back toward 2 percent over the medium term.	23	2

201509	2596	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We have to be more aggressive than that.	23	2
201509	2597	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We want to be actually back to 2 percent.	23	2
201509	2598	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And, as President Evans suggested, taking into account the closeness to the effective lower bound, we might want to be willing to have some overshooting in the medium term in terms of our modal inflation outlook, just to guard against those downside risks.	23	2
201509	2599	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Several people talked about being concerned about disliking rapid increases in interest rates.	23	2
201509	2600	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Again, this is introducing a non-goal-oriented consideration into your policy decisionmaking.	23	2
201509	2601	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To offer some context, when we’re talking about rapid increases in interest rates, we’re talking about increases faster than 25 basis points a quarter.	23	2

201509	2603	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the Committee—again, as President Evans mentioned—would have a better alignment between its medium-term outlook and its long-run objectives by waiting and then raising rates at a slightly faster pace.	23	2
201509	2604	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Something more like the 2004–06 pace, which I believe was actually viewed as fairly measured, would deliver a better outcome.	23	2
201509	2605	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The next few meetings and the decisionmaking around liftoff are really critical not just for the course of policy in the near term and how it’s going to affect the economy, but also in terms of setting up the strategic framework of how the Committee is going to think about policy.	23	2
201509	2606	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We continue to be overly influenced by a collection of Taylor-like rules.	23	2
201509	2607	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I suggested yesterday that this had served the Committee extremely poorly during the course of the recovery.	23	2

201509	2609	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It was a meeting in which the Committee had terminated QE1, and was thinking about, how do we best time the removal of accommodation—specifically, the increase of interest rates—with the improvement in the economy so as to best support the recovery?	23	2
201509	2610	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The debate within the Committee, shaped by Taylor rules, had the dovish side in the 8s in terms of the unemployment rate and the hawkish side in the 9s.	23	2
201509	2611	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I was there.	23	2

201509	2613	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is about the problem with our framework that was in place before 2008 imprisoning the Committee into an unduly slow recovery.	23	2

201509	2615	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The way you don’t have that happen again is by conditioning the policy decisions now about liftoff and afterward much more firmly on the outlook for prices and employment and by building in, I think, risk protections along the lines that President Evans has suggested.	23	2
201509	2616	2015-09-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I look at what’s happening in the world, and we look at all of the experiences countries have had in trying to escape the zero lower bound.	23	2

201509	2645	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	23	2
201509	2646	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2647	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I thought we had an exceptionally interesting discussion yesterday, and I’d like to start by reflecting on it.	23	2
201509	2648	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Broadly speaking, two sets of views were expressed, and they were also mentioned by the Chair in her opening remarks this morning.	23	2
201509	2649	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The first set of views starts from the two criteria we specified earlier this year that would have to be met before we first raise the interest rate.	23	2
201509	2650	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The criteria we set out were, first, that there be further progress in the strengthening of the labor market and, second, that members of the Committee believe with reasonable confidence that the inflation rate will reach 2 percent in the medium term.	23	2
201509	2651	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	As I explained yesterday, I believe we’ve met those criteria.	23	2
201509	2652	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	To justify that view, one has to explain why, when the actual inflation rate is so far from 2 percent, we can say that we’ve met those criteria.	23	2
201509	2653	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The explanation is simple—that the current low inflation rate is due largely to declines in the price of oil and to the appreciation of the exchange rate, both of which are temporary.	23	2
201509	2654	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	By the calculation I described yesterday—which takes into account not only the difference between the actual and core PCE price deflators, but also the indirect effects on the inflation rate of the decline in the price of oil and of the exchange rate—the underlying inflation rate is approximately 1.6 percent at present.	23	2
201509	2655	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	To be sure, those two criteria are only necessary conditions for raising the interest rate.	23	2
201509	2656	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I’ll say more on that later, for I’ll end by making the case that we can delay raising the federal funds rate beyond the end of this month, but that if current conditions continue, we should raise the federal funds rate before the end of the year.	23	2
201509	2657	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The second set of views starts from the fact that there is no inflation in sight, and that we should not raise the interest rate even though, in the view of many, the labor market is close to the natural rate of unemployment.	23	2
201509	2658	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Rather, we should stay at the effective lower bound, possibly allow the unemployment rate to decline below the natural rate, and raise the interest rate only when we clearly need to deal with the inflation rate, which, if we were writing for the newspapers, we’d say is “when we see the whites of the eyes of inflation.”	23	2
201509	2659	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	In this view, we can and should wait before raising the federal funds rate either because the natural rate of unemployment has fallen to well below 5 percent or because we can allow the actual rate of unemployment to fall below the natural rate and thus contribute to dealing with aspects of the labor market that are not yet at what we think is their normal condition—we’re talking about the participation rate, the long-term unemployment ratio, and part-time employment for economic reasons.	23	2
201509	2660	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	When we reach reasonable levels of those variables, we can raise the interest rate and move toward the natural rate of unemployment from below.	23	2
201509	2661	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I think it’s important to note that, at least in my view, the explicit adoption of such an approach would be widely viewed as a change in the FOMC’s monetary policy strategy.	23	2
201509	2662	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Now, both of these views have merit.	23	2
201509	2663	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The choice between them has been complicated by developments abroad.	23	2
201509	2664	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Just over a month ago, on August 11, China devalued its exchange rate rather clumsily and after a Shanghai stock market bubble had burst.	23	2
201509	2665	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	And there was a bubble.	23	2
201509	2666	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Even the governor of the Chinese central bank described it thus.	23	2
201509	2667	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The Chinese exchange rate move created shock waves, one of which arrived at the New York Stock Exchange on August 24, when the Dow Jones index declined in the morning by over 1,000 points and then closed down by 588 points, about 3.8 percent.	23	2
201509	2668	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	By the way, I wonder whether we’re not going to have sharper, more rapid changes in prices in the stock markets as electronic trading develops further.	23	2
201509	2669	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Subsequently, emerging market and developing-country problems, many of which had started well before the Chinese devaluation, began to draw the attention of markets in the industrialized world.	23	2
201509	2670	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	For example, the Brazilian economy is in trouble.	23	2
201509	2671	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The Russian economy is doing badly.	23	2
201509	2672	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	So are other countries in Latin America.	23	2
201509	2673	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	So are some countries in Southeast Asia and Africa, and even Canada and Australia are suffering from effects of the declines in the price of oil and of other commodities.	23	2
201509	2674	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Less mentioned are the improvements in the euro zone, the fact that the United Kingdom’s economy is moving ahead well, the expectation that the Indian economy will grow this year at over 7 percent, and the possibility that India is going to be the China of the next I-don’t-know-how-many years.	23	2
201509	2675	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	What are we to do?	23	2
201509	2676	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Well, the choice between going now and going soon is very close.	23	2
201509	2677	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	In light of the genuine uncertainty caused by the Chinese devaluation and the subsequent realization that there were other difficulties in the global economy, I can support not raising the interest rate now and waiting until either October or December to raise the rate.	23	2
201509	2678	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I’ve got a series of observations on our discussion that I can’t figure out where to put in this statement at a logical place.	23	2
201509	2679	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	So I’ll talk about them now, and, if they’re out of order, you’ll make the appropriate corrections and let me know what they are so that I can improve this in retrospect.	23	2
201509	2680	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	First, we’re all very concerned about the problems in foreign economies.	23	2
201509	2681	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	When I listen to them, they sound much larger than what I found in the Tealbook in terms of their effects on the US economy.	23	2
201509	2682	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I think the Tealbook forecast was made in full knowledge of the situation in the global economy, and we can be sure that the staff attempted to take into account the quantitative effects of the external situation on the US economy.	23	2
201509	2683	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I do believe it appropriate that, besides expressing our worries about foreign economies and describing links between their economies and ours, we should try to make a quantitative estimate of how large those effects are likely to be.	23	2
201509	2684	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	These are, admittedly, early days, but the evidence so far is that those effects will not derail the impressive recovery of the United States’ economy since 2009, where, in particular, the labor market has continued to strengthen at a remarkably steady—indeed, impressive—pace.	23	2
201509	2685	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The next comment I’m going to make is that one keeps hearing about this “unduly slow” recovery.	23	2
201509	2686	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t think it’s unduly slow.	23	2
201509	2687	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I think it’s remarkable, in fact, what has happened to the unemployment rate.	23	2
201509	2688	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	If you’re thinking about GDP, that hasn’t recovered.	23	2
201509	2689	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	But the difference between what’s happening to labor and what’s happening to GDP is productivity, and I don’t think monetary policy is responsible for that.	23	2
201509	2690	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I have a few other points.	23	2
201509	2691	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	We keep saying we will look through supply shocks, but we don’t.	23	2
201509	2692	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	We keep talking about how low the inflation rate is.	23	2
201509	2693	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is largely a result of two large supply shocks, and we’d better remember that we look through supply shocks when one day we find inflation above 2 percent because of supply shocks.	23	2
201509	2694	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	We also tend to forget that we have a cushion of 40 basis points as a result of the enlarged balance sheet, as the discussion yesterday of the effects of beginning to run off our portfolio made clear.	23	2
201509	2695	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Another point is, remember that the price of housing is high because we put the interest rate very low.	23	2
201509	2696	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	So it may not be a sign of a pathology.	23	2
201509	2697	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	It may be a sign of health that monetary policy worked as planned.	23	2
201509	2698	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	That, nonetheless, does mean that there’s possibly going to be some pain when we start raising interest rates from the housing market.	23	2
201509	2699	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	There are two more things in the collection of random—but not totally random— observations.	23	2
201509	2700	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Regarding the question of whether the real wage should start rising independent of the behavior of productivity is an interesting one.	23	2
201509	2701	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I’ve had some discussions with people who say, “Well, tell me where productivity comes into the Phillips curve.”	23	2
201509	2702	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Productivity comes in, in fact, in a way that was mentioned yesterday by Governor Powell and, I believe, by someone on the other side of the table—probably President Williams.	23	2
201509	2703	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Productivity affects the demand for labor, and that’s where it comes in.	23	2
201509	2704	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Finally, this is not a scientific observation, but this is one that is useful to remember.	23	2
201509	2705	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I think that the experience of what happens when stock prices begin to go down or when something goes wrong in the financial markets is summarized by something Warren Buffett said, which I’m sure is more correctly attributed to someone else.	23	2
201509	2706	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	You know, in the United Kingdom, everything was said by Shakespeare or Churchill.	23	2
201509	2707	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	In France, it was de Gaulle.	23	2
201509	2708	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	In the United States, it’s Lincoln or Buffett.	23	2
201509	2709	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	[Laughter]	23	2
201509	2710	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Buffett said that when the tide goes out, you see who’s been swimming naked.	23	2
201509	2711	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	And mostly, as you start unwinding some excitement in the financial markets, you discover that there’s a whole lot more that’s been going on than you knew about.	23	2
201509	2712	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is something that gives me pause when we say, “Well, we’re not seeing much in the way of problems right now.”	23	2
201509	2713	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	But that’s a general comment.	23	2
201509	2714	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I clearly support alternative B.	23	2
201509	2715	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	But I’d like to add that, while we may not yet be at the maximum-employment level and are certainly not at the target inflation rate, I think we can soon comfortably start, and should start, the gradual process of returning to a normal stance of monetary policy.	23	2
201509	2716	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I would like to deal with one issue that is frequently mentioned at this point in the discussion.	23	2
201509	2717	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	It’s that of the foreign central banks that raised the interest rate prematurely.	23	2
201509	2718	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Well, I know one of those examples very well.	23	2
201509	2719	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The Bank of Israel was the first central bank to raise its interest rate in 2009.	23	2
201509	2720	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	It raised the rate from 50 basis points to 75 basis points.	23	2
201509	2721	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	It did that because the economy was growing and inflation was above the target range, largely due to the fact that housing prices were rising rapidly.	23	2
201509	2722	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	It stayed on this path of raising rates until they reached about 3 percent, when the European crisis developed and the effect of the Federal Reserve’s QE, which had begun after the Bank of Israel had raised the rate, began to become obvious.	23	2
201509	2723	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is to say, they followed Keynes’s advice—when the circumstances changed, we changed policy.	23	2
201509	2724	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	That’s what I think has happened in most of these cases.	23	2
201509	2725	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I regard the proof that if you raise the rate, you’re going to raise it too early as not recognizing the dynamics of what was happening in the global economy, where 2009, as was mentioned yesterday, looked like the end of the recession for many.	23	2
201509	2726	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Then, sometime around 2010, we began to realize that, actually, it was more complicated than that and we had to do more.	23	2
201509	2727	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I could say the United States reversed policy.	23	2
201509	2728	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Why?	23	2
201509	2729	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	It invented QE.	23	2
201509	2730	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	So it also cut interest rates.	23	2
201509	2731	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t think that that example is worth a whole lot, though it’s become part of, certainly, what I read in the newspapers whenever I see a discussion of this.	23	2
201509	2732	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Now I’ve spoken for too long, but I’m going to speak a little bit longer.	23	2
201509	2733	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Once we become more confident that the global economy is not at the start of a serious crisis, and that the external effect on US economic activity and inflation of foreign developments is likely to be subdued, I believe we should get started.	23	2
201509	2734	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I gave a lot of reasons for that in the July meeting.	23	2
201509	2735	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	In the interest of saving time, I won’t repeat all of them now.	23	2
201509	2736	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	But let me briefly mention four of the main reasons, with apologies for repeating myself.	23	2
201509	2737	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	First, monetary policy will continue to be very expansionary even after we start moving, for we are not about to lift off vertically.	23	2
201509	2738	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	We are about to begin the process of gradual normalization.	23	2
201509	2739	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I recommend that we think very hard about the assertions made by even highly respected economists and policymakers that raising the federal funds rate at this meeting or in the near future could be an epochal mistake and realize that they’re almost certain to be wrong.	23	2
201509	2740	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Even after we make our first move, monetary policy will be extremely expansionary.	23	2
201509	2741	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Furthermore, this will be a surprise to no one, and many around the world agree that this change should come soon.	23	2
201509	2742	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Some in the emerging market countries even want it as soon as possible.	23	2
201509	2743	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Second, we’ve now held the nominal interest rate at its effective lower bound for six years and nine months.	23	2
201509	2744	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	In so doing, we’re sending a signal that the situation in the US economy is still extremely far from being normal.	23	2
201509	2745	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The interest rate aside, I do not believe that is the current situation.	23	2
201509	2746	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	If the Federal Reserve sends a well-reasoned signal that we think the US economy is now strong enough to begin normalizing, we would be providing an important boost to confidence of businesses and households.	23	2
201509	2747	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	That’s something the Chair mentioned as a possibility in her opening statement.	23	2
201509	2748	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	The improvement in confidence would have a positive effect on spending and job creation.	23	2
201509	2749	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Third—and this is also an important point—beginning normalization when we’ve met the criteria that we’ve set out to meet will enhance the credibility of the FOMC.	23	2
201509	2750	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Conversely, if we continue to delay despite meeting these criteria, market participants and Fed watchers will not know what to make of our communications, and our credibility will suffer.	23	2
201509	2751	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Now, there is a statement that has recently been made that practically any argument that’s made on the basis of credibility is bound to be wrong.	23	2
201509	2752	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	I think that, while we should always examine arguments that rely on credibility with suspicion, credibility really matters for a central bank, particularly for the most important central bank in the world.	23	2
201509	2753	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	In this regard, I have considerable sympathy with President Lockhart’s view that the markets need to understand better what we intend to do.	23	2
201509	2754	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	One of the best ways to achieve that is by doing what we have said we will do.	23	2
201509	2755	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Fourth, the decisions we make this year are going to affect the economy next year and after that, so we need to be moving our policy stance with future conditions in mind.	23	2
201509	2756	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	If the situation in foreign economies stabilizes—note that I am not saying “if foreign economies stabilize,” just “if their situation stabilizes”—and if, as the SEP suggests, most of us agree that we should start normalization this year, we need to think about whether to start it in October or December.	23	2
201509	2757	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	There is an attraction to the idea of going in October, because, if the objective situation so justifies, that would demonstrate to the public that we can, indeed, make decisions eight times a year, not just four times—at press conference meetings.	23	2
201509	2758	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	But, of course, I do understand the preference of not a few FOMC members for December.	23	2
201509	2759	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	To conclude, I support alternative B and believe that in our statements, we should emphasize that we stand by our frequently repeated statement that we expect the beginning of normalization to occur in 2015.	23	2
201509	2760	2015-09-17	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201509	2793	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	This is the old Roseanne Roseannadanna line on Saturday Night Live:  “It’s always something.”	23	2

201509	2802	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Quite apart from economics, I believe we can all think of things that, 30 years ago, were regarded as normal and natural, but that we today regard as aberrant.	23	2

201509	2834	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Do they have a timetable?	23	2
201509	2835	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Every other meeting?	23	2
201509	2836	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Every meeting?	23	2
201509	2837	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Every third meeting?	23	2
201509	2838	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Every fourth and a half meeting?	23	2
201509	2839	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	What is their presumption here?”	23	2
201509	2840	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	So I don’t think we’re going to escape those issues.	23	2
201509	2841	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Finally, on language, I agree with President Lockhart’s top-level point but disagree with the second point.	23	2
201509	2842	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	The top-level point is, it would be good if, even internally, we could get some more agreement and then possibly communicate it externally.	23	2
201509	2843	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Where I differ, for the reason I said a minute ago, is in the articulation that we’re reasonably confident that inflation is there.	23	2
201509	2844	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	The improvement in the labor market is a more or less objective thing.	23	2
201509	2845	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	You can argue whether there is enough progress here or there.	23	2
201509	2846	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But either there is or there isn’t.	23	2
201509	2847	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think that, to many people, the reasonable confidence about inflation has come down to, “Look, we just think we’re close enough to eliminating slack that it’s going to start happening.”	23	2
201509	2848	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	That may not be irrational, but it’s still highly subjective, and it’s hard as a basis for coming together on something that we can agree on, even internally, as a trigger.	23	2
201509	2849	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	But I definitely think it would be worth the effort.	23	2
201509	2850	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	Regarding President George’s comments, I couldn’t agree more.	23	2
201509	2851	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to the data point issue, we do not want the world thinking, “Their decision turns on whether the next employment report is 210,000 jobs or 140,000 jobs.”	23	2
201509	2852	2015-09-17	meeting	TARULLO	That’s just not where we want to be.	23	2

201509	2856	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	23	2
201509	2857	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2858	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I will support alternative B today as written.	23	2
201509	2859	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	For me, this has been a close call, and I do think you can make the case in a pretty strong form on either side of this decision for today.	23	2
201509	2860	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	In fact, that’s exactly what the Chair did in her opening remarks.	23	2
201509	2861	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	The Committee has guided markets to expect liftoff by the end of this year, subject to incoming data.	23	2
201509	2862	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	Those data have been, on balance, perhaps a little better than expected.	23	2
201509	2863	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	But we have additional disinflationary forces arriving, albeit ones we view as transitory, and a higher risk of a global slowdown.	23	2
201509	2864	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	In addition, US financial conditions have tightened since the July meeting by well more than 25 basis points, according to well-publicized external estimates.	23	2
201509	2865	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	So there’s no sense of the Committee getting behind the curve.	23	2
201509	2866	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	To me, it makes sense to defer liftoff for this meeting to let both the inflation picture and the global situation settle down.	23	2
201509	2867	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I do not view the situation as it exists today as justifying a lengthy delay before liftoff.	23	2
201509	2868	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I don’t see a need to see the rates of inflation or nominal wage growth rising prior to our liftoff.	23	2
201509	2869	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I would be satisfied with at least some reasonable stability in the dollar, so that we could be sure that the recurring temporary factors holding down inflation are finally abating.	23	2
201509	2870	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I would, of course, also need to see continuing growth to support ongoing tightening in the economy.	23	2
201509	2871	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	Frankly, if real GDP growth is strong enough, then I might be persuaded to lift off even in the absence of other factors.	23	2
201509	2872	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	Turning briefly to the Committee’s two-part test for liftoff: I view the first part of the test—some further improvement in the labor market—as met for this meeting.	23	2
201509	2873	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	There’s been substantial improvement in the labor market.	23	2
201509	2874	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	And, while there’s no doubt additional slack, unemployment is now at or near most estimates of the natural rate.	23	2
201509	2875	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	Even if the natural rate— either the short-term rate or the longer-term rate—is significantly lower than current estimates, which is a distinct possibility, we’re already on a path, it seems to me, to unemployment in the mid-to-low 4s by the end of 2016.	23	2
201509	2876	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	So, from this perspective solely, I think it’s getting to be about time to start raising interest rates.But the inflation test is more complicated.	23	2
201509	2877	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	In the Tealbook baseline, inflation returns to 1.9 percent in 2018, which, one might argue, is itself a decent argument that the test is met.	23	2
201509	2878	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	After all, the test is appropriately about the medium term.	23	2
201509	2879	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	But today inflation is not just well below the 2 percent objective.	23	2
201509	2880	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	It’s also very likely to decline in the coming months, albeit due to factors we view as transitory.	23	2
201509	2881	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	So declaring the inflation test to be met would require the Committee to look through a substantial transition period and place a great deal of weight on the Phillips curve.	23	2
201509	2882	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	To put it simply, intermeeting developments have not increased my confidence of inflation moving toward 2 percent in the medium term.	23	2
201509	2883	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I see this as a problem, and I see a risk of sending a signal to markets that the Committee is not serious about the 2 percent objective.	23	2
201509	2884	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	For me, delaying liftoff for a meeting or two may provide some evidence that we’re serious about reaching the 2 percent objective and allow time to understand the evolution of global developments.	23	2
201509	2885	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	There’s been some discussion of a so-called dovish raise, whereby the Committee would raise interest rates at this meeting or a subsequent meeting, but then wait for some time to let the effects settle in.	23	2
201509	2886	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	The sense of this is that the Committee’s communications have been confusing to the markets—you hear this from market participants quite a bit—and that we’re, in effect, getting in the way of the economy now, as the Chair referenced in her remarks, and causing trouble in the markets.	23	2
201509	2887	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	That will become increasingly the case if uncertainty increases, and we ought to just lift off get it over with.	23	2
201509	2888	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	Now, I don’t support that approach at this meeting, but I do think that if either the October meeting or the December meeting provides a reasonable opportunity to go ahead and lift off, I would be inclined to look very carefully at that and take it, if possible.	23	2
201509	2889	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	We had a chart today that Thomas presented that showed the distribution of expected timing of liftoff by FOMC meeting.	23	2
201509	2890	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I’d really like to see the likelihood of liftoff be way north of 50 percent by the time we lift off.	23	2
201509	2891	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	In fact, in my perfect world, it would be 100 percent.	23	2
201509	2892	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	But I realize that’s not likely in a world in which the Committee is of different views and in which we’re being very data driven.	23	2
201509	2893	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	I’d still like to see that be much higher than 50 percent, and I think it would be very unwise to lift off at a time when the market is not expecting it.	23	2
201509	2894	2015-09-17	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2895	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201509	2896	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	23	2
201509	2897	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2898	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Well, I appreciate the opportunity to hear from all but one member of the Committee, and many of the considerations that have been, I think, very eloquently put on the table on both sides of this debate also affect my own judgment about the appropriate policy rate path.	23	2
201509	2899	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	As many of you have stated, in recent months, domestic real activity has expanded at a resilient pace.	23	2
201509	2900	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	We’ve seen improvement in consumption, growth, housing, and the labor market.	23	2
201509	2901	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The U-3 measure of unemployment has declined further, suggesting a reduction in labor market slack, although the absence of any firming in any wage or compensation measures suggests that some slack remains on other margins, such as participation and involuntary part-time employment.	23	2
201509	2902	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	By contrast, headline inflation has moved further away from our target during the intermeeting period.	23	2
201509	2903	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Market-based measures of inflation expectations have again drifted down, and the 12-month change in core PCE inflation appears stubbornly mired at around 1¼ percent, where it has been for some years now.	23	2
201509	2904	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	These developments lead me to conclude we are likely still in the quadrant of inflation– resource utilization space in which both our full employment and inflation objectives are consistent with accommodation.	23	2
201509	2905	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I sense some concern that, by continuing accommodation at current levels, the economy could soon breach resource constraints.	23	2
201509	2906	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	But there is a risk associated with that approach, in light of the fact that monetary policy acts with a lag, and that it may lead to a buildup of inflationary pressures, a rise in inflation expectations, and, consequently, persistent inflation materially in excess of our 2 percent target.	23	2
201509	2907	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	However, the persistent and sizable deflationary forces from the international environment, the estimated small effect of resource utilization on inflation, the persistence of core inflation materially below our 2 percent target, and the important gravitational force of inflation expectations suggest that this risk is likely still to be relatively modest.	23	2
201509	2908	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Financial markets appear to agree with that judgment.	23	2
201509	2909	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Perhaps most important, we have substantial policy space for addressing this risk.	23	2
201509	2910	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Thus, while it is important to remain vigilant with regard to the possibility of an unexpected emergence of inflationary pressures, I believe that, at present, we should place considerably more weight on a different risk—that the underlying momentum in the domestic economy is not strong enough to withstand the considerable deflationary pull of the international environment.	23	2
201509	2911	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In these circumstances, by tightening prematurely, we risk falling short of both our inflation and full employment targets over the medium term.	23	2
201509	2912	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Indeed, for those who believe that a hike of 25 basis points might be warranted in September, macro models at the Board and elsewhere suggest that intermeeting international developments alone have produced a notable tightening in US financial conditions roughly equivalent to an increase of 50 basis points in the federal funds rate.	23	2
201509	2913	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And it’s important to underscore that most of that—indeed, almost all of it—comes from exchange rate movements and not from movements in equity markets or domestic financial markets that may prove temporary.	23	2
201509	2914	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, as I discussed yesterday, the risks to the US outlook from additional international headwinds are weighted to the downside.	23	2
201509	2915	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	China appears to be only partway through a complicated adjustment of its exchange rate regime and broader financial market reforms, and it faces considerable challenges regarding the clarity of communications as well as piercing the fog surrounding its macroeconomic data.	23	2
201509	2916	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In these circumstances, any further policy moves could prompt a broader reassessment of underlying fundamentals that could, in turn, be amplified by real or perceived linkages to the exchange rates of other important economies in their neighborhood as well as to important commodity producers.	23	2
201509	2917	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In that regard, as has been noted, two of our closest trade partners, Canada and Mexico, have already seen sizable currency depreciations.	23	2
201509	2918	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I view these effects on the US economy as likely to be relatively persistent.	23	2
201509	2919	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Indeed, over the past year, we’ve seen a strong feedback loop between expectations of policy divergence between the US and our major trade partners, and financial tightening that takes place through exchange rate and financial market channels, which front-runs our policy process.	23	2
201509	2920	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, my reading of the risks is informed by the large majority of episodes in recent years in which policy tightening in other advanced economies, prompted by improving domestic activity, was soon followed by a reversal of policy and, in several important cases, subsequent migration to the effective lower bound and beyond.	23	2
201509	2921	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Those episodes have all proved costly.	23	2
201509	2922	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I think we could find only one exception, Iceland, which has several very special features as a result of their financial crisis.	23	2
201509	2923	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, from the perspective of risk management, we have considerably greater latitude to adjust the path of policy in response to higher-than-expected inflation than we have to provide additional accommodation in response to additional financial tightening.	23	2
201509	2924	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In light of that—both the substantial financial tightening that has taken place and its likely effect on the outlook, the additional downside risks that could materialize from global developments, and the asymmetry of risk-management considerations—the risks of moving prematurely seem to me to outweigh the risks of waiting.	23	2
201509	2925	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Alternative B provides a nice summary of the Committee’s outlook and how that is likely to condition the policy rate path for the period ahead.	23	2
201509	2926	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Paragraph 1 provides a good description of recent developments, contrasting the reassuring growth in the many domestic components of aggregate demand and progress on employment with considerable softness in net exports and the additional restraint on headline inflation and market-based measures of inflation expectations.	23	2
201509	2927	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I would note that the one important piece of information missing from this paragraph that certainly informs my thinking is the soft indicators that have come in across the board on compensation.	23	2
201509	2928	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I strongly support the sentence in paragraph 2 that describes the implications of developments abroad for risk considerations.	23	2
201509	2929	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I think it’s important to acknowledge that foreign developments are a key risk to the achievement of our objectives.	23	2
201509	2930	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Inclusion of this language enhances the clarity of our communications by informing observers that we are paying attention to these developments because of their potential effect, through many channels, on the US outlook.	23	2
201509	2931	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	My own judgment is that recent global developments and possible future developments pose downside risks to the outlook, but I can support the more neutral language and alternative B more generally.	23	2
201509	2932	2015-09-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201509	2933	2015-09-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
